Education Broadcasting Supplement

How to Promote Rural Sidelines (Middle)

— Qian Tianhe, Deputy Director of the Central Agricultural Experiment Station

Currently, our arable land, although felt to be insufficient, still has abandoned open space. Isn't this a contradictory phenomenon? No, because this open space either isn't easily suitable for growing crops, resulting in gains not covering losses, or the space is too small to be willing to cultivate. The former includes barren mountains and river beaches, while the latter includes spaces beside roads and surrounding vacant land. For example, we can use these places to plant castor beans. Castor beans don't discriminate between fertile and barren land and can be left to grow freely, while the castor oil market has great demand. Not only is it used as medicine, but its industrial applications are also increasing day by day. It certainly won't be oversupplied in the short term, so it's a good way for farmers to make a living. This is the third reason for promoting rural sidelines. (4) Processing Agricultural Products What do we mean by processing agricultural products? Let's take an obvious example: cotton is an agricultural product, and after spinning and weaving, it becomes yarn and cloth. This spinning and weaving is called processing. We feel that many agricultural products, such as fruits and vegetables, will spoil if they can't be sold in time. If they can be processed and manufactured, either pickled with salt or made into canned goods, and sold in the market, it will be possible to earn an extra sum. Everyone has eaten raisins, but most of them are foreign products. So why aren't we cultivating them extensively in our country, which is very suitable for cultivation? The biggest reason is that everyone isn't finding ways to process and manufacture them. Bumper harvests of rice and wheat turning into disasters are a common phenomenon in our country. If they can be processed and manufactured into wine, the wine can be sold for money, and the lees can be used to feed livestock, and the livestock can also be sold for money. The surplus labor can be used, and income can be increased considerably. Straw is fuel, but if it's processed and woven into straw sandals or twisted into straw ropes, its economic value will also definitely increase considerably. There are also many agricultural products that aren't worth much money, but after processing, their value will suddenly increase several times. For example, straw hats. Their raw materials are very cheap, but after they're made, they can be sold for one yuan to dozens of yuan each. Therefore, processing agricultural products that can be processed or are worth processing is also a good rural sideline. This is the fourth reason for promoting rural sidelines.

(5) Recovering Lost Revenue Since China opened up trade with foreign countries, foreign goods have gradually occupied our country's market. At first, it was limited to big cities, but in recent years, due to the development of roads and other reasons, foreign goods have gradually penetrated into the countryside. Not only have the original local goods been defeated by them, reducing income for farmers, but farmers have also had an extra expense, accelerating their bankruptcy. According to the agricultural report in the eighth issue of the fourth volume of the Central Agricultural Experiment Station, based on the reports of more than 6,000 agricultural reporters in 22 provinces nationwide in April 1935, farm households that purchased foreign cloth accounted for 30% of all farmers, and those using woolen fabrics accounted for 9.6% of the total. On average, each middle-class farm household in the 22 provinces needed 6.8 jin of foreign sugar and 27.3 jin of kerosene per year. In the past, all these supplies could be self-sufficient, but now they have to rely on foreign goods. With such a large loss every year, how can the countryside not be in slight bankruptcy, and how can the country not be impoverished?

Moreover, there are many local goods that China originally had. Why are they being squeezed out by foreign goods? It's not that the people love to use foreign goods; it's really because local goods aren't strong, not beautiful, or the value is too high. Therefore, we should now improve the original local goods, making them strong and beautiful, and making them cheaper than foreign goods. The sales channels can naturally be slowly restored. For example, Wuxi clay figurines are very famous, but outside of Wuxi, it's not easy to see them. What we see are foreign figures of people, birds, and animals made of chemical materials, which are both beautiful and inexpensive, so the sales channels are very good. What's the reason? It's that the people who make clay figurines in Wuxi aren't willing to research improvements, change the patterns, strive for beauty and low prices, and pay attention to sales methods. If the people who make clay figurines in Wuxi can strive to improve on the one hand and find ways to open up sales channels on the other, we believe that they can definitely reduce a portion of imported children's toys. There are also many new sidelines that can be promoted and are effective because the market needs them. For example, Japan exports 4 million goldfish to foreign countries every year, worth 500,000 yuan. Especially in the United States, the sales channels are the widest because Americans have money and goldfish are very fun to play with, so this good business has been completely occupied by the clever Japanese. But our country has paid little attention to this sideline so far. For example, the wives of professors at Yenching University in Beiping use ramie fabric as raw materials to teach women in the rural areas of Beiping to weave all kinds of tablecloths and table mats. Westerners like these tablecloths and table mats very much. Almost everyone who goes to visit the school buys a few to take back. But there are no sales outlets for these tablecloths and table mats that meet the psychology of Westerners in places with many Westerners, such as Shanghai. If "Jiangxi, Sichuan, and other provinces that originally produced ramie fabric use the farmers' spare time and labor to promote the weaving of tablecloths and table mats, in addition to supplying Westerners in China and so-called high-class Chinese for purchase, they can also be sold to the West. Isn't this a way to recover some of the lost revenue? This is the fifth reason for promoting rural sidelines.

The five reasons for promoting rural sidelines have already been stated, but to summarize, it's all for the sake of increasing the income of farmers. Because the foundation of the country is built on farmers, and if farmers' livelihoods aren't prosperous, it will be very difficult for the country to become prosperous!

3. How to Promote Rural Sidelines

(1) Prerequisites for promoting rural sidelines:

(A) It must be able to truly connect with the industrial sector This topic seems difficult to understand at first glance, but it's actually very simple. Now let's give a few examples to illustrate: For example, silk. Farmers raise silkworms and sell the cocoons to silk factories for reeling silk. This has a history of many years. But in the past few years, silk prices plummeted, many silk factories closed down, and the cocoons that farmers worked hard to harvest sold for too little money, making them feel that the gains didn't cover the losses. Many farmers resentfully chopped down mulberry trees and stopped raising silkworms. Last year, silk prices suddenly soared, and silk factories all opened up, but there was a shortage of raw materials, and some silk factories still had to close. This situation was indeed affected by the world economy, but a lack of communication with each other was also a major reason. For example, matchboxes are mostly contracted out to poor families in the city by match factories. The living standards of poor families in the city are high, and the wages paid by match factories are low, so they are constantly complaining. If it were entrusted to rural areas, the living standards in the countryside would be low, and farmers could use their spare time, and there would be more people. The wages wouldn't need to be increased, and the output could be increased rapidly. Farmers would have a stable sideline and could earn a certain income. It would be a real benefit for both sides. Therefore, if we want to promote sidelines, we must be able to connect with the industrial sector.

(B) It must meet market needs and have the possibility of expanding sales channels When we promote rural sidelines, we must see whether the products of this sideline meet market needs and whether there is the possibility of expanding sales channels. For example, weaving native cloth as a sideline. Now the native cloth market has been encroached upon by foreign cloth and machine-woven cloth. If we blindly promote it, it will definitely fail. For example, castor oil. The market needs it very much now, and we are making every effort to promote the cultivation of castor beans to meet the demand, so of course we will only make a profit. This is the result of the former not meeting market needs and the latter meeting market needs. For example, weaving cattail bags in salt-producing areas. These cattail bags are specially used for packing salt. We think that the number of cattail bags used for packing salt every year is very large, so we vigorously promote weaving them. The output has increased, but in addition to packing salt, there are no sales channels for other reasons, such as inconvenient transportation and the lack of sales organizations. This kind of promotion will definitely fail. But if we manufacture paper umbrellas, the sales channels for paper umbrellas have not only been strong domestically in recent years, but exports have also been increasing day by day. We hope that this sideline will have great hope if we promote and improve it. This is a real example of the former having narrow sales channels and being difficult to expand, and the latter having broad sales channels and being expandable.

Page 7

League of Nations Council Passes Opium Report; Expresses Gratification at China's Anti-Smoking Plan; Ironclad Evidence Obtained of Japanese Drug Trafficking

(Geneva) The League of Nations Council held a public meeting today and passed a report on the opium trade, expressing keen concern for the situation in China. The report stated that there is now clear evidence that opium production is being carried out on a large scale both north and south of the Great Wall, and that foreigners are secretly manufacturing and widely distributing narcotic drugs. The Council expressed satisfaction with the Chinese government's six-year plan to ban opium planting and smoking. The report mentioned Japan, stating that there is now ironclad evidence that people are engaged in organized drug trafficking, especially of "Heroin" manufactured in Japan, in North America, India, and other parts of the Far East. (20th Reuters dispatch)

(Geneva) The League of Nations Council held a closed meeting again at about 5:00 PM. The Romanian Foreign Minister, Mr. Antonescu, proposed that the Council appoint British Lord Hailey as a member of the League of Nations Mandates Commission. At 5:15 PM, the Council held a public meeting, the 93rd session of the Council, chaired by the Argentine Foreign Minister, Mr. Lamas. The Italian representative was still absent. The public meeting today was very short, with only the Portuguese representative, Mr. de Vasconcelos, presenting a report on the work of the Opium Committee and the Committee on the Prohibition of Narcotics, which was quite optimistic. The whole meeting unanimously approved the report, and the Council adjourned at 6:00 PM. The date of the next meeting has not been set, but the General Assembly of the League of Nations is scheduled to open at 10:00 AM next Monday. According to custom, the opening ceremony of the General Assembly must be held in the afternoon, but this decision was made to advance it in particular. It is expected that after the opening of the General Assembly, the Credentials Committee will work quickly to decide on the issue of whether the Abyssinian delegation can attend. (19th Havas dispatch)

Hopeful that China Will Be Elected as a Semi-Permanent Member

(Nanjing) The 17th General Assembly of the League of Nations will be held in Geneva on the 21st. Our representatives Gu Weijun, Guo Taiqi, and Jin Wensi have arrived one after another. The agenda of the General Assembly will first be addressed by the acting chairman, who will describe the achievements of the League of Nations over the past year and hopes for the future, followed by the election of the official chairman and vice-chairmen. Among the issues to be discussed, the only one related to us is the issue of China becoming a semi-permanent member, which is generally expected to pass. As for amending the Covenant, our government has sent a written opinion. According to those familiar with diplomacy, it is imperative that the League of Nations increase its organizational strength. At the same time, the voice of Italy's return to the League of Nations has been realized. However, amending the Covenant is the first amendment to the League's own organization since its establishment and cannot be determined in a hasty time. It will generally be referred to the First Committee (discussing legal matters) for lengthy exchange of views. The General Assembly, according to past practice, has six committees and a special committee of the agenda committee. This year, it is said that it will discuss the general issue of international economic coordination. (20th Dispatch)

German Propaganda Minister Visits Greece

Athens The German Propaganda Minister Goebbels, arrived here today. He plans to stay at a hotel in the suburbs. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs will regularly send a secretary to accompany him. Center of European Political Activity Shifts to Geneva; League of Nations General Assembly Opens Today; Major Issues of Disarmament, Economy, and Covenant Amendment to Seek International Coordination

(Geneva) The center of European political activity will shift to Geneva tomorrow, as the League of Nations General Assembly will open on this day in a very threatening environment and hold important meetings. The Spanish civil war, the war talks in Nuremberg and Moscow, the world's frenzy of rearmament, and the tense situation in Palestine will all be ominous backgrounds for the General Assembly's discussions. However, it seems that none of these serious issues will be raised for direct discussion. In order to make the General Assembly aim at one goal in addition to its usual work, the French government plans to urge the members to take joint action on the three major issues of disarmament, economic rectification, and League of Nations reform. Regarding disarmament, the first step seems to be to re-establish the Third Committee of the League of Nations General Assembly, which has not met since 1932. The second issue is economic rectification, and French economists are quite optimistic about the prospects for this. They believe that it is urgent today to reconvene an international conference to seek the restoration of the free flow of trade and the stability of currency exchange rates. As for the League of Nations reform plan, the General Assembly has now received 18 written opinions, which will be submitted to the First Committee for separate consideration after a general discussion. (20th Reuters dispatch)

Powerful British Delegation Departs for Geneva; Eden Lays Over in Paris for a Short Stay

(London) The main figures of the British delegation have departed from London for Geneva. This is one of the most powerful British delegations ever sent to Geneva. The delegation includes Dominion Minister Malcolm MacDonald, Financial Secretary to the Treasury Morrison (Mr. Morrison served as chairman of the International Committee for the Implementation of the Non-Intervention Agreement in the Spanish Civil War), and Lord Cranborne of the Foreign Office, who has arrived in Geneva to represent Britain at the League of Nations Council meeting. In addition, there is also Lord Privy Seal and Leader of the House of Lords Halifax, who is scheduled to depart from London today. The head of the delegation, Foreign Secretary Eden, will first fly to Paris today and then take a train to Geneva at night. (Paris) British Foreign Secretary Eden and his wife left London at 3:10 PM today and immediately went to the Prime Minister's Office to meet with Prime Minister Blum to discuss the international situation. (20th Havas dispatch)

The Abyssinian Issue at the League: Lengthy Credentials Review, Rome Expresses Firm Opposition

(Geneva) When the 17th regular session of the League of Nations General Assembly opens tomorrow morning, it will immediately appoint a "Credentials Committee" to review the credentials of representatives from various countries. The credentials of the Abyssinian representative will be the most troublesome, and it is unknown whether they will be considered valid. The expected solutions are no more than three: (1) Recognize the Abyssinian representative's credentials as valid, but this is highly unreliable. (2) If the committee's opinions are inconsistent, two reports should be prepared, one representing the majority opinion and the other the minority opinion, both to be submitted to the General Assembly for discussion, or a statement that the matter is of a purely political nature, to be handled by the General Assembly. (3) The Abyssinian representative's credentials are deemed invalid. Regarding this point, the Abyssinian delegation, or another delegation, may make a request, and be supported by other countries, to submit the case to the International Court of Justice in The Hague to determine whether denying the Abyssinian Emperor's appointed representative the right to attend raises the issue of non-recognition of the government formed by the Emperor. In addition, there is another matter, whose political implication, though weaker, is equally difficult to handle: the selection of the "Credentials Committee" members. According to the rules of procedure of the League of Nations General Assembly, this committee should be composed of eight members. Currently, England, France, Peru, and Hungary have already submitted their candidacy. It is yet to be determined whether other countries will step forward to fill the remaining four seats. In short, tomorrow's meeting is bound to be interesting, and the League of Nations General Assembly, in order to allow the committee sufficient time to deliberate and draft a report, will likely postpone the discussion of this report until tomorrow afternoon. (Havas, 20th)

(Rome) Noted journalist Gaeta, mouthpiece of Prime Minister Mussolini, recently published an article in the Italian Daily, stating: "As long as the Abyssinian delegation is in Geneva, Italy will not participate in the work of the League of Nations. The Abyssinian regime has now been overthrown forever. Italy does not seek recognition from others for its sovereignty over that land, but if a group of exiles emerges to represent this regime, Italy cannot recognize it. Italy has now occupied Abyssinia and will continue to occupy it without hesitation. This is the main fact. Other countries' recognition is crucial to us, even more so than it is to other countries, because if other countries do not clearly recognize the system that Italy is implementing in Abyssinia, Italy will not recognize the rights and interests that other countries enjoy in Abyssinia." His conclusion was: "Some say that the Italian Empire must expand outwards and that it will harm the interests of other European countries, regardless of size or strength. This is absolutely incorrect. However, Italy will act differently if it is forced by other countries." (Havas, 20th)

Re-allocation of Colonies: Poland Desires a Share, Requests a Seat on the Mandates Commission, Poland and Romania Aim to Strengthen Old Alliance

(Paris) A "Journal" reporter, Saint-Brice, recently declared that Polish Foreign Minister Colonel Beck has submitted a request to the League of Nations, stating that his country should serve as a member of the League of Nations Mandates Commission. Locarno Conference: Italy's Conditions for Participation, Mediterranean Issue Must Be Resolved First, British Note Does Not Offer Any New Proposals

(Rome) The "Battaglia Padana" recently published an editorial stating, "Italy's participation in the Five-Power Locarno Conference should, at present, take the resolution of the Mediterranean issue as a prerequisite, because the situation in the Mediterranean has changed greatly since Italy conquered Abyssinia. The United Kingdom previously attempted to establish a collective security system but failed. Now it is inviting Italy to participate in a regional security plan (referring to the New Locarno Pact), and this region is geographically unrelated to Italy. According to diplomatic tradition, the most urgent issues are the various consequences directly arising from the war. Now, after the end of the Abyssinian War, the most pressing issue is the Mediterranean issue, not the Western European issue. If the Mediterranean issue is not resolved, Geneva has not yet made a legal settlement on Italy's conquest of Abyssinia, and the United Kingdom's policy towards the Red Sea, which is controlled by Italy, is still undecided. How can Italy participate in the New Locarno Conference under such circumstances? From this perspective, the preparations for the Five-Power Conference must still be awaited." (Havas, 19th)

The Rise and Fall of the Austrian Heimwehr: Originally a Paramilitary Group, Now Sharing the Fate of the German Stahlhelm

(Vienna) Since the Vienna branch of the Patriotic Heimwehr requested the reinstatement of former Interior Minister Major Fey as the leader of the branch, internal disputes have arisen. Our reporter recently reported on the history and current status of the Heimwehr. The Patriotic Heimwehr was founded in 1919 and was originally a purely paramilitary group. Its purpose was to resist Yugoslavia's attempt to re-incorporate part of Carinthia, which was ceded to Yugoslavia after the war, into Austrian territory. It then became a political civic group. At that time, the Heimwehr's provincial branches acted independently and had no central organization. It was not until 1932, after the former cabinet advisor, Prince Starhemberg, the leader of the Home Guard, and his political friends reorganized it, that they united and restored its original paramilitary nature. Since then, the group has played an important role politically, competing with the Social Democratic Party's Schutzbund. Later, the Schutzbund gradually lost ground and was finally dissolved along with the Social Democratic Party in 1933. As for the Heimwehr, it assisted former Chancellor Dollfuss with force in dealing with the Social Democratic Party and the National Socialist Party during the Social Democratic Party incident in February 1934. Dollfuss' position was thus consolidated, and the foreign and financial policies he advocated were able to succeed. When current Chancellor Schuschnigg succeeded as Prime Minister, he began to organize the Patriotic Front and eradicated all paramilitary groups. This move was a fatal blow to the Patriotic Heimwehr. To this day, the Heimwehr has practically ceased to exist. In addition, there are deep disagreements between Prince Starhemberg and the leaders of the provincial branches. It is expected that the group will meet the same fate as the German Stahlhelm and withdraw from the political and military stage. (Havas, 20th)

It is expected that a squadron or two of the Royal Air Force will soon be stationed in Hong Kong to cooperate with Singapore. Smith will visit Vietnam, the Philippines, British North Borneo, and Sarawak when he flies back to Singapore from Hong Kong. Smith will inspect the recently built military airfield in Sarawak. Currently, government troops are bombing the fortress with explosives, and the fighting is becoming increasingly fierce. (Reuters, 20th)

Attacking Ancient Fortress with Fire: Government Troops Use Gasoline in Combat

Toledo. After the commander of the government troops attacking the Alcázar fortress ordered the use of gasoline in combat, the ruins of the fortress are now surrounded by thick smoke and flames. Today, firefighters dug trenches around the fortress, poured thousands of gallons of gasoline into them, and then ignited them with bombs. Instantly, the flames soared into the sky and were impossible to approach. At the same time, bullets rained down on the fortress. In the midst of this tension, a brave man from the rebels rushed out from the rain of bullets, seized the oil hose from the firefighters, and poured it towards the government troops. However, he was shot all over his body, fell to the ground, and died. This plan to attack with fire still failed to allow the government troops to occupy the fortress, so the government troops stopped using this tactic. Some of the rebels later attempted to break through, but were driven back by a barrage of gunfire, with many casualties. Now, the explosives of the Asturias miners have blasted a gap in the wall of the fortress. Government troops have installed machine guns at the gap, preparing for a decisive attack. (Reuters, 20th)

Toledo. Although the Alcázar fortress here has been mined and destroyed by government troops, the rebels are still putting up a final stubborn resistance. The bloody battle between the two sides has not stopped. Last night, rebels from the palace attacked the former Governor-General's office to the left of the Alcázar through a tunnel, setting up machine guns for defense. At dawn today, the government mobilized the assault teams and bomb squads of the "Iberian Anarchist Federation" to continue the attack with a large number of hand grenades and bombs. Government General Asensio arrived here last night and found a way to burn down the left corner of the Alcázar and the Governor-General's office without any danger. The method was to use two large water trucks filled with gasoline, connected by a long cloth pipe. The oil pipe passed through the roof of the Santa Cruz Monastery. After the soldiers lit the end of the pipe, they poured it into the Governor-General's office. Just as the oil pipe reached the front of the building, it was spotted by the rebels inside. The rebels bravely seized the oil pipe and changed its direction, making it shoot towards the government side. However, because the government troops fired with rifles, the rebels holding the oil pipe were shot down before long. The rebels inside the building then went downstairs, launching a surprise attack on the government troops with rifles and machine guns. After the government troops threw hand grenades, the rebels retreated. There were many rebel deaths, but no government troops died. Until noon, the battle was very fierce, with bombs exploding everywhere. The rebels were forced to abandon the roof of the Governor-General's office and guard it with machine guns on the ground. Government troops also rebuilt the ramparts and used cannons to shoot at the Governor-General's office. At this time, the rebels retreated into the building, and the sound of gunfire subsided. Government troops seized the opportunity to move forward, dig a hole in the wall, and throw bombs into the building. However, because the walls were very thick, the damage from the bombing was not very great. Currently, the rebels have completely stopped firing. Government troops are seizing the opportunity to aim machine guns at all the doors of the office. When the Havas News Agency reporter left Toledo, it was nearly dusk. The whole city was filled with smoke, and although it had been raining heavily all day, the fighting had not stopped. Today, the reporter witnessed another extremely cruel scene. A militiaman of the government army said to the reporter, "Do you want to see a cruel scene? Please come with me." The reporter followed the militiaman and entered a coffee shop opened by a Swiss man at the corner of the Sagador Square near the Governor-General's office. The militiaman then took me up a bullet-scarred ladder to a window upstairs, where I saw a window with iron bars on the opposite Alcázar Palace ruin. A woman was shouting inside the bars, "Comrades, save my life! Please, for the sake of your mother, let me out! Without these iron bars, I would rather jump down and commit suicide!" She called for help for half an hour, but the militiaman was unable to get close to the window to rescue her. When the woman became exhausted, she stopped shouting and waved her hand outside the iron bars for help. Soon, the woman disappeared. The reporter and the militiaman did not notice whether she had fallen to the ground after being shot or had been forced to leave the window by the rebels who had spotted her. (Havas, 19th)

Hurricane on the US Atlantic Coast Turns Northeast; Material Losses of 500 Million Yuan

Renowned British-Australian Air Race Pilot Black Killed in Accident; Collision with Military Aircraft in Fog; Critically Injured and Unable to be Saved

(London) Renowned British aviator Mr. Black, who won the British-Australian Air Race in 1934 with Mr. Scott, has joined the London to Johannesburg Air Race scheduled for September 29th. Today, while piloting the "Lady Liverpool" at the Liverpool Speke Airport, it was struck by an air force bomber, causing the propeller to hit and critically injure Black in the cockpit. At the time, the fog was dense, and Black's plane was black and white, making it difficult for the bomber pilot to distinguish. This is likely the cause of the accident. Black was rushed to the hospital after being injured, but despite the best efforts of the doctors, he died from his injuries. Black's wife is actress Thea Sistman. She was rehearsing a new play in a London theater when she received the news of her husband's death. In 1934, Black and Scott flew a plane together from Mildenhall, England, to Melbourne, Australia, in 2 days, 22 hours, and 58 minutes, a distance of 11,323 miles. As a result, they won the £10,000 prize from Australian millionaire Sir Robertson, and became famous in the aviation world. Black was initially in love with Ms. Sistman, and after arriving in Melbourne and completing his great achievement, he telegraphed her to propose. She telegraphed back her acceptance, and they became a couple. (Reuters, 19th)

Prominent Figure in Tsarist Russian Literature, Tang Qian'ge, Dies in Prague

Prague, Czech Republic: Tang Qian'ge, a famous writer of the Tsarist Russian era, recently died here at the age of 92. Tang Qian'ge was born in 1844 in Tallinn, Russian Empire. In his early years, he gained fame in the literary world by publishing works about the Arctic Ocean. During the Russo-Turkish War in 1877, Tang Qian'ge accompanied the Russian commander General Skobelev on the expedition, personally went to the front lines, and described the realities of the war. He also participated in the battle of the Shipka Pass, making him known throughout Russia. He later served as a war correspondent for various newspapers for 50 years. Tang Qian'ge personally participated in every major war in Europe. Although he was old, he regretted not being able to personally witness the recent war between Italy and Abyssinia. Tang Qian'ge was also a famous novelist, and together with Nekrasov, Dostoevsky, Tolstoy, and Gorky, he was one of the most famous writers of the era of Tsar Alexander II, advocating liberalism and opposing autocratic politics. Gorky passed away not long ago, and now Tang Qian'ge has also passed away, leaving the veteran figure in Northern Tsarist Russian literature completely gone. (Havas, 19th)

The Possibility of Anglo-Japanese Amity

—Ji Nan

In recent months, the call for Anglo-Japanese amity has grown louder. In early September, Tokyo even rumored that British Foreign Secretary Hoare had drafted an Anglo-Japanese compromise plan: (1) Britain recognizes "Manchukuo" and Japan's special status in North China; (2) Japan respects China's territorial integrity, maintains the Open Door policy, and British vested interests in China. Although this news was denied by London authorities, judging from the recent large-scale activities of Japanese Ambassador to Britain Yoshida Shigeru in London and the remarks of Londoners, Anglo-Japanese amity, although not yet ripe, seems to be an undeniable fact that both sides are interested in adjusting bilateral relations. The recent visit to Japan by the new British Ambassador to China, Sir Hughe Knatchbull-Hugessen, en route to his post, to meet with Japanese diplomatic authorities and discuss Anglo-Japanese issues and Sino-Japanese diplomatic issues, is further proof of this. If we observe the past relationship between the two countries and the current international situation, it is not difficult to see what the possibility of Anglo-Japanese amity is.

During the Russo-Japanese War, Britain and Japan were allied countries. At that time, Japan's power was not yet fully developed. It was trying to expand outward but lacked support. Britain's Far Eastern forces were being threatened by old Russia. Although it wanted to resist, it was unwilling to sacrifice itself. Therefore, they used each other and formed an alliance to defeat their common enemy. However, after old Russia was defeated, Japan rose up in its place. It expanded vast territories politically, increased its military strength, and made great progress in industry. Thus, the foundation of capitalism was established. After the European War, Japan achieved even more amazing achievements in industry and commerce, inflicting a great blow on Britain's economic power in the Far East. In Australia, India, Canada, China, Southeast Asia, and other places, Britain and Japan were in a position of direct conflict in commerce. For twenty years, there have been open and secret struggles, without ceasing, and the so-called Anglo-Japanese alliance is only a historical relic. After the September 18th Incident, Japan exclusively occupied the Northeast Provinces. Last year, it further coveted Hebei and Chahar, creating its special status in North China. Thus, Britain's economic power in China was further suppressed. The so-called special trade of smuggling penetrated everywhere, and Japan's economic war against Britain in South China and the Yangtze River basin was even more pressing, causing Britain to feel that its power in China was not only greatly threatened, but also in danger of fundamental upheaval. Under these circumstances, if it wants to take a tough stance against Japan to maintain its inherent position in China, the European continent is restless due to the rising arrogance of Fascist countries, and it has no time to take care of the Far Eastern issue. In this distress, Britain has been trying to break this stalemate for a year.

So what is the way to break this stalemate? It is either to compromise with Japan or to join hands with the Soviet Union. In September last year, British economic envoy Sir Frederick Leith-Ross came to China to investigate the economic situation and help us reform the currency system. At the same time, he also had full hopes for the adjustment of Anglo-Japanese relations. However, at that time, Japan's desire to exclusively occupy China was rising day by day, so Ross spent half a month in China, visited Japan twice, and was subjected to cold ridicule by the Japanese government and public. He had to return in vain, and there was no improvement in Anglo-Japanese relations. However, if something is lost in the east, it may be recovered in the west. Anglo-Soviet cooperation can also be a great threat to Japan. Compared with the situation at the time of the Russo-Japanese War, the positions of Japan and Russia have obviously been reversed. Today, Britain's alliance with Russia to contain Japan can also be said to be inevitable. Therefore, although there has been a permanent barrier between Britain and the Soviet Union for years due to the absolute incompatibility of national systems, and Britain has even led the world's anti-Soviet front, due to the gradually deepening contradiction between Britain and Japan, the increasingly acute conflict, and the slim hope of compromise, it had to change its course and urgently seek improvement. As a result, the Anglo-Soviet loan agreement and the Anglo-Soviet naval agreement, which had been brewing for several months, suddenly took a sharp turn for the worse at the end of July and were declared established under Britain's great step. The former is a harbinger of Anglo-Soviet economic understanding and cooperation, and the latter recognizes the Soviet Union's reserved conditions for the Far East, giving the Soviet Union the right to freely respond in the Far East. The subtext is nothing more than to explain that Britain is about to support the Soviet Union to confront Japan.

The Anglo-Soviet cooperation having been initiated, people in Tokyo deeply felt that Britain's gradual hardening towards Japan would make Japan's diplomatic isolation even worse. Foreign Minister Arita's repeated statements revealed anxiety, so Japanese public opinion loudly advocated Anglo-Japanese amity, and Ambassador Yoshida Shigeru was active in London. However, the emergence of this kind of pro-British atmosphere in Japan, which was not seen during Ross's repeated visits to Japan, is not only due to the Anglo-Soviet cooperation and hardening towards Japan, but also due to the recent trend of China towards real unification and the gradual progress of political and economic construction. This is also an important factor. Today, China's real unification has been completed, so Japan's attitude towards China should be clearly established as soon as possible. Since it is impossible to monopolize East Asia, the urgent need to adjust bilateral relations is almost inevitable. Many insightful people in Japan have already paid attention to this, so there is a call to re-establish a policy towards China. After Ambassador Kawagoe arrived in China, he strongly advocated Sino-Japanese economic cooperation. Foreign Minister Arita also admitted that it is necessary to emphasize "economic diplomacy." Japan's policy toward China is shifting from the military to the diplomatic, and from the political to the economic. If this is clear, then Japan's conflict of interest with Britain in China, due to the development of this new situation, must strive to seek a reasonable solution at this time.

But what is Britain's attitude? Will it always pursue a consistent policy of joining hands with the Soviet Union to contain Japan? That is not the case. After all, diplomatic skills are multifaceted, and British diplomacy is known for its flexibility and adaptability to the environment. Moreover, Britain only wants to maintain its inherent economic power in China and not be threatened. On August 8th, the new British Ambassador to China, Sir Hughe Knatchbull-Hugessen, firmly stated in Tokyo in response to a question from a Central News Agency reporter: "Britain's greatest interest in China is to maintain peace and trade. Therefore, Britain will consider anything that causes disturbance and unrest in any part of China to hinder Britain's interest." If Japan can give considerable satisfaction in this regard, there is no reason why the relations between the two countries cannot be temporarily compromised. In other words, the focus of the problem is whether Japan can make concessions in its economic war against Britain. However, Japan's amazing progress in industry in recent years has forced it to find overseas markets to dump its surplus goods. The increasingly fierce trade wars between Japan and India are also unavoidable. Whether Japan can make concessions to Britain is actually still a matter of doubt. In summary, the possibility of Anglo-Japanese amity depends on how much Japan can guarantee Britain's economic power in the Far East, that is, how many economic concessions Japan will make to Britain.

Realization of Peace in Guangxi; Li Zongren Flies to Guangzhou to Meet Chiang; Bai Chongxi Stays in Guangxi to Handle Troop Demobilization; Martial Law Begins to be Lifted in Wuzhou; Guangxi Currency Appreciates

Guangzhou Correspondence: The mediation of the Guangxi situation, after half a month of negotiations between the two sides, was specifically resolved in the middle of this month. Li Zongren and Bai Chongxi took office as Pacification Commissioners and members of the Standing Committee of the Central Military Commission on the 16th in the Guangxi Provincial Party Headquarters. Cheng Qian and Huang Shaohong were sent by the central government to administer the oath. After Li and Bai took office, Bai Chongxi was unable to come to Guangzhou to meet with Chairman Chiang for a while due to the need to handle the demobilization of the Guangxi army and the retirement of the militia in Guangxi. Therefore, Li Zongren first went to pay his respects to Chiang and ask for instructions on the future pacification of Guangxi Province. Li Zongren then flew east from Yongning on the 17th with Guangxi Provincial Chairman Huang Xuchu, Guangxi Army Staff Officer Liu Weizhang, and Military Commission Staff Officer Lei Biao, and Cheng Qian and Huang Shaohong, who came to Yongning to welcome them, in a giant aircraft. At about 3 pm, the aircraft landed safely at Tianhe Airport. At that time, those who welcomed them at the scene included Ju Zheng, Qian Dajun, Yu Hanmou, Huang Musong, Xu Jingting, Xiang Hanping, and senior party and government officials of Guangdong Province. After Li Zongren, Cheng, Huang, Liu, Lei, and others got off the plane, Li shook hands with each of the welcomers as a courtesy. Li was wearing a gray cloth military uniform that day and was in very good spirits. After leaving the airport, he went to the banquet of Yu Hanmou and Huang Musong, which did not end until about 5 pm. Li Zongren returned to his residence at the Jiyuan residence in Dongshan that night to rest and received his subordinates in Guangdong. The next day (the 18th) at about 9 am, Chairman Chiang, accompanied by Qian Dajun, drove from Huangpu to Li's residence in Dongshan to visit Li. Li, having received prior notice, immediately went down the stairs to greet him with Cheng Qian, Huang Xuchu, Huang Shaohong, and others. After Chiang and Li met, they went into the hall and talked for 30 minutes before Chiang left and went to the Huangpu Military Academy to discuss party and state affairs. After breakfast, Li Zongren accompanied Liu Weizhang, Cheng Qian, Huang Xuchu, Huang Shaohong, and their entourage in four cars along Zhongshan Road to Yuzhuwei in Panyu, crossed the river to the Huangpu Military Academy, and paid his respects to Chairman Chiang. They discussed the overall situation and the party, military, and political issues of Guangxi Province in detail. At about 2 pm, Li returned to his residence by car to rest for a while, and at 3 pm, he drove to pay a return visit to the Guangdong military and political officials Yu Hanmou and Huang Musong. It is heard that Li Zongren and Huang Xuchu will stay in Guangdong for a few days. After asking for instructions on the post-war affairs of Guangxi Province, they will return to Guangxi. The Guangxi Pacification Office is organized in accordance with the regulations promulgated by the central government. Regarding the number of Guangxi troops reorganized, Weng Zhaoyuan's division will be incorporated into the Guangxi army, but the designation will be changed to the Fifth Route Army. The military expenses will be 2.5 million to 3 million yuan per month, half of which will be assisted by the central government. It is planned to change the new name on October 1st. Li Zongren will serve as the commander-in-chief of the Fifth Route Army, and Li Pinxian will serve as the chief of staff. This order can be issued during the day. The Fifth Column of the Guangxi Army, Weng Zhaoyuan's troops, stationed in Beihai will withdraw from Beihai in a few days and return to Yulin on the Guangxi border to await orders. Cai Tingkai has already left Yongning and went to Yulin on the 16th to inspect his old troops and prepare for the reorganization. Wuzhou began to lift martial law from the 17th, and the troops are also preparing to demobilize. The civilian ships that were requisitioned a few days ago have been given funds to return. The mines on the Fu River and the Dajiang River are also being recovered one after another, and water and land transportation will be restored. The value of Guangxi banknotes has rebounded. Previously, 100 Hong Kong dollars could buy 200 Guangxi dollars. After the 16th, 100 Hong Kong dollars were only worth 168 Guangxi dollars. After the realization of peace, it will not be difficult for Guangxi banknotes to return to their original value. (September 19th)

Li Qingxuan Negotiates New Tax Measures with the Hebei-Chahar Authorities; Inspection Office Still Secretly Clearing Smuggled Goods; Recent Shipments of Smuggled Goods to Pingbao Increased Sharply

Tianjin Correspondence: Li Qingxuan, a counselor of the Ministry of Finance, accompanied by Advisor Qi and two Western tax officials from the Shanghai General Customs Office, arrived in Tianjin on the morning of the 16th. At noon, they attended a banquet hosted by Sun Weidong, the Tianjin Customs Superintendent, and met with Guo Zhihan, the director of the Finance Department of the Hebei-Chahar Council, Wang Hongen, the director of the Hebei-Chahar General Inspection Office, and Xu Liya, the Tianjin Customs Commissioner. They exchanged detailed opinions on anti-smuggling and the collection of inspection fees in Hebei and Chahar. Li explained the Ministry of Finance's views on these two matters, and the discussions were lengthy. On the morning of the 17th, Li and Sun visited Song at No. 113, 17th Road, British Concession, conveying the financial aspirations for the new Hebei-Chahar tax. Song made sincere expressions. In the afternoon, Li visited Zhang Zizhong, the mayor of Tianjin, and Wang Hongen, the director of the Hebei-Chahar General Office, successively, seeking information. That evening, Qin Dechun and Ge Dingyuan were summoned to Tianjin by Song. Together with Guo Zhihan, Wang Hongen, and others, they went to Bei Ning's residence on Haihe Road, inviting Li Qingxuan to continue discussions. After reaching a result, Li telegraphed the Finance Ministry, awaiting a reply. Upon receiving the reply, it will be conveyed to Song for a final decision. Li himself will go to Ping to investigate after completing his tasks in Tianjin. Regarding the negotiations in the North, Li issued a written statement on the 18th, stating that he was ordered to come north with customs tax officials because Chairman Song and others discussed the situation in the Tianjin market last month and instructed him to report back to Minister Kong. After review by the relevant departments, they are now bringing it to Chairman Song for further consultation. Yesterday, they met with Chairman Song and reported on the progress. Regarding the original proposed plan, they were instructed to further study it with all relevant personnel to find a suitable way to maintain the legitimate interests of Chinese and foreign merchants, resolve the current difficulties, and allow the North China economy to move towards activity. The motive for this trip north is not solely about the Hebei-Chahar Inspection Office. The Hebei-Chahar Inspection Office was reorganized from the Gun and Salt Coastal Defense Inspection Office. This office has been established for a long time, originally to investigate bandits, drugs, and munitions, and to assist in anti-smuggling, not to collect consumption taxes on smuggled goods. Recent foreign reports that the office has announced regulations to collect one-eighth of customs duties and release smuggled goods are mostly misunderstandings and speculation. Now that the truth is clear, this issue no longer needs to be studied. Regarding the Hebei-Chahar General Inspection Office, since its establishment on the 8th of this month, due to excessive opposition from foreign parties and repeated inquiries from Shanghai groups, those in charge have become timid and dare not publicly announce tax rates. However, actual work has already begun. The Pingbao Qikou sub-offices were established last week. Only the Zhangjiakou, Shijiazhuang, and Cangxian sub-offices are still being organized. Wang Hongen, the director-general, is the strongest advocate for active implementation. He is horrified by the accusations from various parties and has secretly inspected and released all staff, using smugglers and merchants as guarantors to register the amount of goods for future total fees. On the 16th, one release of smuggled goods included 13,000 bags of sugar and 300 boxes of rayon. At a certain concession, there are 8,000 bags of sugar and 1,300 boxes of rayon being inspected and awaiting shipment. Other items such as seafood, foreign wine, kerosene, and textiles are also awaiting shipment in large quantities. Although the amount of fees was set in advance, it has changed due to the high level of opposition. It is now proposed to divide them into four grades: Heaven, Earth, Xuan, and Huang, and levy them at different rates of 60%, 45%, 35%, and 25% of the regular customs duty. However, smugglers disagree with the increase because the office promised in advance to collect only one-eighth of the customs duty. The person in charge is finding it difficult. The Tianjin Customs and the office are targeting the three card stations in the suburbs of Tianjin, which have been set up in Baimiao Xiaoxiyingmen and Shengfang Wharf. However, in recent days, they have intercepted large quantities of smuggled goods. Smugglers have produced the "Hebei-Chahar Cangyan Ports Coastal Defense Inspection Office" inspection certificates as proof of payment of regular taxes, and they are not subject to inspection or detention, and they rush through the checkpoints. Every day, dozens of trucks transport these goods and forcibly pass through the checkpoints. Smuggled goods without inspection certificates, with military flags inserted on the trucks, also pass through the checkpoints, transporting them to Pingbao and southern Hebei. Because the customs needs the assistance of the Hebei-Chahar military and police agencies, they are taking advantage of Li Qingxuan's presence in Tianjin to ask him to negotiate on their behalf to ensure strict interception. (18th)

Kunshan: Bandits Attempt to Rob, Arrested

The Public Security Bureau recently received a secret report that a group of bandits would come to Kunshan to plot something illegal. Detective Li of the Detective Team led the entire team of detectives and police to the station at about 7:00 AM on the 18th. They saw a group of people resembling workers, accompanied by a woman, getting off the train. Li and others followed closely behind, all the way to the vicinity of the Xiaoximen Confucian Temple, before issuing an order to arrest the five men and women involved. They were taken to the bureau, and a Browning pistol and twenty rounds of ammunition were found. After interrogation, they confessed their names as Wang A..., Wu Guangyou, Zhu Weiqing, Zhou Zhengrong, and the female bandit Gu Zhangshi. They admitted that they came to Kunshan with the intention of robbing the family of a certain surname in the Leek Field in the city. The five bandits, along with the guns and ammunition, were transferred to the judiciary for investigation.

Wuxi: Five Notorious Robbers Arrested

Song Taowei, captain of the water patrol team of the Public Security Bureau of this county, recently received a secret report from informants stating that Tao Jinshan (the younger brother of Tao Yalin, the ringleader of the Chen Xiangchun family case in Xiaozhangjiaqiao, which was solved during the tenure of the former detective team leader Zhong Jihe), and several other escaped robbers who had robbed Longzhu Nunnery in Zhoujing Township, were hiding in the countryside near Hushuguan in Suzhou. After receiving the report, Captain Song, accompanied by patrol officer Wang Hengru, traveled by car to Hushuguan the day before yesterday and submitted a letter to the Fourth Branch of the Public Security Bureau of Yang County, requesting assistance in the arrest. Director Xu of the branch dispatched patrol officer Hu and several police officers to go with Captain Song to search the areas of Baitishan and Beiyangyangbang. They successfully arrested the bandits Tao Jinshan and the female bandit Tao Zhu. They also captured a bandit in his thirties in the Tang Fuquan teahouse on North Gate Street of Hushuguan. In a straw shed across the river from the Wenchang Pavilion, they captured the robber Xu Furong. Two rifles, one Browning pistol, one bayonet, and one 1,000-foot flashlight were found in the home of Yao Gantou Zhu Tianshou. Zhu himself escaped, and only his mother was captured. In addition, they also seized men's and women's leather clothing, iron bars, and other stolen goods and weapons. Another pistol was carried by the bandit leader Tao Atan when he escaped. The captured male and female bandits were escorted to Wuxi yesterday (20th) and sent to the Public Security Bureau for transfer to the local court for trial.

Zhenjiang: Opening of the Provincial Federation of Commerce

The fifth member congress of the Jiangsu Provincial Federation of Commerce is scheduled to open today (20th) at 10:00 AM in the Zhenjiang Chamber of Commerce Building. As of 6:00 PM yesterday, the number of registered delegates was 138, and the actual number of delegates who had arrived was more than 30. More than 30 proposals have been received. After the opening ceremony, the proposal review meeting will be held in the afternoon. Eight Bathhouses Ordered to Close

The Zhenjiang County Government, in accordance with orders to inspect the boiler equipment in the bathhouses of the provincial capital, previously dispatched personnel to conduct inspections and notified the relevant bathhouses of the points that should be improved, setting a deadline for all to complete the renovations. Those who failed to comply would be ordered to close. Now that the deadline has passed for half a month, eight bathhouses, including Xinquan, Second Spring, Central Bathhouse, Xiyuan, Daguan Garden, Zhenjiang Bathhouse, Daxingchi, and Runquan, have not yet complied. After receiving the report, the county government believed that the bathhouses were intentionally delaying and should be strictly enforced as a warning. They were ordered to close in accordance with the case and have sent a letter to the Public Security Bureau of the provincial capital to assist in the execution yesterday.

Floating Corpse Found at Baota Bridge

A male corpse, about twenty years old, was found floating at Baota Bridge on the South Dou Outer Canal on the 19th. Taizhou: Security Team Cracks Ransom Case

Wang Hua, the head of the Aohuan self-funded security team in Wenling County, learned at 3:00 AM on the 16th that Zhang Bao's house in Zhaimen was hiding a kidnapped person. He immediately led soldiers to the house. A bandit was discovered and ordered to guard the doorway. Wang entered the house and encountered a bandit upstairs. The two sides exchanged gunfire. As a result, the bandit Zheng Xuebin was killed, and the bandit Zheng Hualiang was injured. The kidnapped person, Wang Mingrui, a resident of Qinggang, 54 years old, was found. He was led by the local Zhu Xisu Bao and, at 2:00 PM, sent the injured bandit, the bandit's wife, Zhang Zhengshi, and two pistols to the county government for strict handling.

Huzhou: Carelessness at Yuansheng Warehouse in Yangxiang Lane

The Yuansheng goods warehouse behind Yangxiang Lane in this city suddenly caught fire at about 2:30 AM this morning (19th). The warehouse staff heard the noise and got up to see that the fire had spread through the roof. Yilong from various districts rushed to the scene to rescue, but because it was too far from the river wharf and the location was narrow, it was difficult to rescue. The fire was extinguished after burning for an hour. As a result, Xintai Salted Goods Warehouse and the Salt Industry Association were affected. All the salted fish, cured meat, and means of making a living were burned to ashes, and more than 20 houses were burned, for a total loss of more than 10,000 yuan.

Tongshan: Robbery at the School Military Field

The school military field in the west of Tongyi is a place where miscellaneous people gather in the west of the city. There are many cattle and donkey merchants. Yuan Chengen, the owner of the Sishun public cattle firm, lives in Chengjia Lane nearby. Because of the developed transaction, he has a little savings. He also handles the storage of cash for buying and selling cattle and donkeys on behalf of customers. At 9:00 PM on the 17th, Yuan was still at the store and had not returned home. His wife, Zhang, was breastfeeding in the room when four bandits, each wearing blue clothes, two holding box guns and one holding a flashlight, broke in through the front door. One person was left on guard at the door, and the other three rushed into the room, extinguished the lights, and used a flashlight to search, scaring Zhang into silence. They searched the room and robbed 460 silver dollars before escaping. When Yuan heard the news, he reported it to the military police to pursue the bandits, but they were nowhere to be found. The Public Security Bureau is currently investigating and arresting the murderers.

Recent Overview of Guangdong and Guangxi (1)

— Our reporter Xiao An

After the renewal of the situation in Guangdong and Guangxi, the people's wealth, the party, and the military were returned to the central government. All the organizations in the southwest in the past few years have completely ended. In the future, the two provinces of Guangdong and Guangxi urgently need the construction of a new administration, and the people of the two provinces are also very eager to recuperate. Therefore, the current situation of the two provinces of Guangdong and Guangxi is of concern to the people of the country. The reporter has a trip to Guangdong and Guangxi, and now records the things I have seen and heard.

From Shanghai to Guangzhou

People traveling between Shanghai and Hong Kong have always relied on postal ships for express journeys, which can be reached in two days and one night. In the past few years, the business situation of various postal ships between Shanghai and Hong Kong, the American Dollar Steamship Company and the British China Navigation Company are the best, followed by the postal ship companies of France, Germany, and Italy, and the Japanese NYK Line is the worst. The reason for this is that the NYK Line business has been greatly affected since the 918 Incident. It is found that the NYK Line's three ships, the Tatsuta Maru, Asama Maru, and Chichibu Maru, are newly constructed and have a load of more than 20,000 tons. The passenger tickets are cheaper than the Dollar and China Navigation companies. Taking the third-class cabin as an example, the Dollar and China Navigation companies are US$15, while the Japanese company is US$10. However, the business performance of the NYK Line is not good. This can be considered more than half. It is heard that in recent years, the NYK Line company has relied on the subsidies issued by its government for survival due to poor business. However, since August 10, the NYK Line passenger ticket has been reduced from US$10 to US$8, intending to attract business by devaluing the price, in order to improve passengers and cargo and reduce the responsibility of its government for relief. However, the Dollar and China Navigation companies, seeing the NYK Line cut prices, also reduced the third-class passenger ticket from US$15 to US$12 from this month to compete with the NYK Line. This shows the situation of Japanese commercial environment.

The reporter took a boat south from Shanghai. On the boat, I saw a few poor old overseas Chinese, and many students returning from Tokyo wearing kimonos all day long. There is nothing else to record. My roommate was Mr. Zhang of Sun Yat-sen University and Mr. Fu, the staff officer of the command. In the two days and nights, we talked in the small room and felt very happy. Mr. Fu participated in the defense against Japan at the Great Wall and the suppression of bandits in southern Anhui and made many contributions to the strategy at the time. Even now, when talking about the Battle of the Great Wall, we still cannot help but sigh. Mr. Fu is a graduate of the Whampoa Military Academy and is proficient in both literary and military strategies. I am very impressed with him. The boat arrived in Hong Kong and docked at the Kowloon pier. The place is close to the Canton-Kowloon Railway, Tsim Sha Tsui Station. The reporter and Mr. Fu and Mr. Zhang took the train to Guangzhou and no longer stayed in Hong Kong. However, the Hong Kong dock workers and the so-called "miscellaneous differences" (the other name of detective) often openly use extortion and other unethical behaviors against the luggage of people going back and forth. The luggage of the reporter and Mr. Fu and Mr. Zhang were merged into one place, and the quantity was slightly more, so they were also blackmailed by them. This kind of fact is a stain on the British civilized politics. The British government should quickly eliminate it.

The Canton-Kowloon Railway express train runs three times a day in both directions. The ones departing from Guangzhou are the Flying Eagle Express at 8:15 AM, the Midday Express at 1:10 PM, and the Flying Dragon Express at 4:50 PM. The ones departing from Hong Kong are the Flying Arrow Express at 8:30 AM, the Midday Express at 12:45 PM, and the Flying Star Express at 5:05 PM. The full fare from Guangzhou to Hong Kong is 1.4 yuan for the third class in Guangdong legal tender, and from Hong Kong to Guangzhou, it is one yuan for the third class in Hong Kong paper money. The exchange rate between the Guangdong currency and the Hong Kong currency is 10 to 14. The other second-class and first-class passenger tickets are calculated in multiples. The reporter took the Flying Star Express to Guangzhou in the afternoon. The Canton-Kowloon Railway, from Hong Kong to Shenzhen, is the British section, and from Shenzhen to Guangzhou is the Chinese section. Along the British section, the British have built many highways. Although the villages are all Chinese style, the layout is very Westernized. The people of Hong Kong call it the "New Territories," which means that the Hong Kong government has newly occupied it. Shenzhen is a Chinese-British border area, and the management of local military and police is relatively loose. The place has become a den of dirt and filth. The three poisons of opium, gambling, and prostitution are all gathered there. The inland bandits also regard the place as a refuge for fugitives. When opium and gambling were not banned, the most famous gambling den was the "Yousheng Company," which was a branch of the Guangzhou Yude Gambling Company. The capital reached more than one million yuan. All kinds of gambling, such as Fan-Tan, Pai Gow, roulette, and dice, are available. The company also built theaters and opium dens to lure gamblers. The harm it leaves to the people is painful. When the train stopped at Shenzhen Station, I looked at the buildings of gambling dens, theaters, and hotels from a distance. The green tiles and pink walls, and the street lights from the station to the gambling dens, theaters, and hotels, all imitate the Forbidden City style, but they are very vulgar. Proceeding beyond Shenzhen, the villages are very dense, but each village must have several watchtowers, standing in the front, back, left, right, or center of the village. The momentum is quite majestic. It is allowed that the Pinghu, Zhangmutou, and Shilong stations are located nearby. Shilong is one of the major towns in Guangdong Province, and also an important road for entering and leaving the East River. The people of the East River have always been known as the strongest in Guangdong. From the walls, you can imagine. At about 8 o'clock, the car arrived at Dashatou Station in Guangzhou.

The Canton-Kowloon Railway Bureau has been vigorously promoting the development of railway affairs in recent years, but the order in the third-class carriages is deeply regretted and has not been improved. The most annoying thing is the hawkers selling food. Some people hold only three or four packages of Yunpian cakes and come and go to sell them more than 20 times. The same is true for those who sell longan, pears, and soda. The inside of the car is very noisy. As for the price, it is even more expensive. Soda sells for 1.4 Hong Kong dollars per bottle, which is equivalent to 20 cents in Chinese currency. Moreover, the clothes of those who sell food are not clean, and the leftovers such as water, vegetables, peels, and shells are discarded in front of the passengers, which is enough to give people a bad impression. The passenger ticket is checked once after the train departs, once again after passing Shenzhen, and then collected by the ticket inspector after passing Shilong. Therefore, when the car arrives at Dashatou Station in Guangzhou, passengers disembark one after another. There is no procedure for collecting tickets at the station. At this time, there are many people gathering on the platform to watch the fun. Chauffeurs and workers carrying luggage also enter the platform directly. This is different from the organization of the Jinghu Railway Station. (Sent from Guangzhou on September 16)

Zhang Gongquan, Yu Feipeng, and Wei Lihuang Arrived in Shanghai on the Same Ship from Hong Kong Yesterday; Mayor Wu, Commander Yang, and Others Went to the Port to Welcome Them; Zhang and Yu Will Return to Nanjing in a Few Days, While Wei Will Transfer Back to Hubei

Zhang Gongquan, Minister of Railways, who went south to inspect railway administration some time ago, Yu Feipeng, Acting Minister of Communications, who inspected communications, and Wei Lihuang, the newly appointed Commander-in-Chief of the Second Route Army, who went to Guangdong from Hubei to pay respects to Chairman Chiang, returned north together on the Canadian Empress of the China Navigation Company after completing their missions. They arrived in Shanghai at about 2:00 PM yesterday and docked at the Gonghexing Wharf on Broadway Road. Those who went to welcome them included Yang Hu, Commander of the Songhu Garrison, Li Dachao, the representative of Mayor Wu, Chu Minyi, member of the Central Committee, Peng Xuepei, Vice Minister of Communications, Cai Jingjun, Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, Huang Boqiao, Director of the Two-Roads Administration Bureau, Cai Zengji, General Manager of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Tan Boying, Deputy General Manager, Li Jingcong, Manager of Eurasia Aviation Corporation, Dai Enji, Manager of China National Aviation Corporation, Zhu Changnian, Acting Superintendent of Jianghai Customs, Pan Guangjiong, Chief Secretary of the Ministry of Railways, Wu Yu, Director of the Municipal Maritime Affairs Bureau, Bao Keyong, Director of the Telegraph Bureau, and Wang Zhinan, Secretary of the Songhu Garrison Headquarters, and more than 40 others. Zhang and Yu will return to Nanjing in a day or two to preside over their respective ministries, and Wei will also go to Nanjing in the next few days and transfer back to Hubei. The talks of Zhang, Yu, and Wei will be recorded separately as follows.

Zhang Gongquan's Talk

According to Zhang Gongquan, his trip south was to inspect the Yuehan Railway administration. The issue of connecting the Yuehan and Canton-Kowloon railways was not discussed. The Yuehan Railway will be officially opened to traffic as soon as military transport is completed. The road will be extended to Huangpu in the future. The estimated cost is 10 million yuan, with the Ministry of Railways and the Guangdong Provincial Government each responsible for 5 million yuan. The rumor that the Ministry of Railways borrowed 3 million yuan from the Shanghai banking community to complete the Yuehan Railway is not accurate.

Yu Feipeng's Talk

According to Yu Feipeng, the communications industry in Guangdong Province, including management, administration, and other aspects, has not been reorganized for more than ten years. On this trip, he inspected all subordinate agencies and drafted a comprehensive reorganization plan to be implemented in order to seek improvement. He also plans to start with the telecommunications administration. Regarding the Shanghai-Guangdong wireless telephone communication, a radio station will be built and actively prepared, and it is expected to be realized within the year.

Zhang Gongquan (International Press Photo)

Yu Feipeng (International Press Photo)

Wei Lihuang's Talk

According to Wei Lihuang, his decision to go south was to pay respects to Chairman Chiang. The current situation in Guangdong and Guangxi is very good. Bai Chongxi is currently in charge of repatriation matters. As soon as it is completed, he will go to Guangdong to pay respects to Chairman Chiang and will go to Nanjing with Chairman Chiang to take office.

Regarding his intention to go abroad, according to his knowledge, Chairman Chiang persuaded him to stay and cancelled the plan. The banditry in Hubei and Anhui provinces has been cleared. Only Henan Province still has a small number of bandits, about several hundred, which can be cleared soon, which is not a problem. He plans to stay in Shanghai for a day or two and then go to Nanjing and transfer back to Hubei.

Good Harvest Year, Cotton Cloth Sells Well, Inventory Sold Out, Production Cannot Meet Demand

In recent years, the domestic cotton cloth industry in Shanghai has suffered from the decline of the rural economy and the dumping of foreign goods, resulting in stagnant production and sales, heavy losses, and a bleak future. According to news from the industry, since the autumn of this year, the sales of domestic cotton cloth have suddenly flourished. Cotton cloth merchants from Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Hubei, Henan, Anhui, Guangdong, Fujian, and other provinces have come to Shanghai to purchase in an endless stream. In the past two months, all the stored cotton cloth in Shanghai has been sold out, and the demand for orders is still strong. Various Chinese textile factories are busy processing and weaving to meet the market demand. This is a phenomenon that the cotton cloth industry has only seen in the past two or three years. The reason for the sudden increase in sales is that this year's cotton, wheat, and silk crops have been plentiful, and the exhausted rural economy has been slightly revived. Therefore, the best-selling cotton cloth is also domestic coarse cloth suitable for rural use.

Public Debt and Savings Deposit Interest Income Tax to be Levied from October 1st; Notice from the Banking Association for Member Banks to Take Note

According to the Sin Sin News Agency, the Shanghai Banking Association, upon receiving an order from the Ministry to levy income tax on public debt and savings deposit interest starting from October 1st, specifically notified all member banks to take note, stating, "Respectfully, we have recently received a letter dated September 7th from the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, regarding a notice. On the 4th of this month, we received Order No. 28774, Series Direct, from the Ministry of Finance, which stated that the Executive Yuan's Order No. 5014 stated that the Minister proposed at the 274th meeting of this Yuan that, having examined the Provisional Income Tax Regulations, which had been

promulgated by the National Government,

[we should] immediately supervise and urge our subordinates to actively prepare. We now, in accordance with the provisions of Article 21 of the said regulations, submit a draft of the implementing rules for approval and implementation. Furthermore, Article 22 of the Provisional Income Tax Regulations stipulates that the date of implementation shall be determined by order. Now that preparations have been completed, the Ministry intends to commence levying taxes from September 1st of this year and requests that a clear order be issued, setting the date of implementation of the said regulations as September 1st of this year. Whether or not this is appropriate should be decided by public vote." The decision was made to refer the matter to the Ministers of Finance, Foreign Affairs, Industry, Education, Transportation, and Railways, and Secretary-General Weng for review. Based on the review opinions reported, the original draft has been revised accordingly. A copy of the revised draft is enclosed for review and instructions. This matter was further submitted to the 275th meeting of this Yuan, where it was resolved: (1) to approve the review opinions and promulgate them immediately; (2) the Provisional Income Tax Regulations and

Implementing Rules

shall both be implemented from October 1st of the 25th year [of the Republic, i.e., 1936]. Furthermore, income from salaries and remuneration of public officials under Category II, and income from public debt and savings deposit interest under Category III, shall be levied starting from October 1st of the 25th year, while all other items shall be levied starting from January 1st of the 26th year [i.e., 1937]. In addition to having the Executive Yuan promulgate the Implementing Rules of the Provisional Income Tax Regulations, to be implemented from October 1st of the 25th year, and issuing a general notice, as well as submitting a report to the National Government for review and record, the directive instructs all subordinate agencies to take note. Furthermore, it requests that the Provisional Income Tax Regulations be promulgated by clear order, setting the date of implementation as October 1st of the 25th year. In addition, it requests that the first three of the four measures decided by the Central Executive Committee to suspend income donations be reviewed and followed. A copy of the Implementing Rules of the Provisional Income Tax Regulations is enclosed for the Ministry to

comply with

and to instruct its subordinates to take note accordingly. This order, etc. A copy of the Implementing Rules of the Provisional Income Tax Regulations has been received by the Ministry. In addition to complying with the instructions and separately informing and instructing [subordinates], we hereby notify you of the date of implementation and the commencement dates for each category, and enclose a copy of the Implementing Rules of the Provisional Income Tax Regulations for your information. Please also instruct your subordinates to comply accordingly, etc. An enclosed copy of the Implementing Rules of the Provisional Income Tax Regulations is forwarded to the Association." Upon receipt of this, in addition to reprinting the Implementing Rules in the September issue, Volume 16, Number 9, of the Association's Commercial Monthly, we hereby record and issue this notice, hoping that you will take note and pass it on for information, etc. With this approval, we are separately notifying each bank in the Association, hoping that you will take note.

Details are recorded as follows:

Party Headquarters Notice

The Municipal Party Headquarters issued a notice yesterday, stating, "Regarding the notice, as the 21st of this month is the sixteenth anniversary of the martyrdom of the late Mr. Zhu Zhixin, this Headquarters will convene a memorial service for representatives from all sectors of society in the auditorium of this Headquarters at 10:00 AM on the same day. Half-Mast Vigilance

Today, all agencies, organizations, schools, and party branches, in addition to sending representatives to participate in the memorial service convened by the Municipal Party Headquarters, will also fly flags at half-mast for one day to express grief.
