National Association of Inspection for Smuggling Requests Ministry of Finance to Facilitate Inventory Sales; Coordinating with Chambers of Commerce to Issue Certificates

The National Association of Inspection for Smuggling yesterday submitted a document to the Ministry of Finance regarding the issuance of inventory certificates by inland chambers of commerce, stating, "Submitting a report with a request for review and instructions. This association has received a report from the Smuggling Inspection Committee of the Hankou General Chamber of Commerce, stating, 'This association has received letters from various trade associations in the city, stating that goods purchased before the implementation of the Transportation and Sales Regulations have all been registered. However, these goods cannot be issued transportation and sales licenses, resulting in obstacles when transported to other locations. Moreover, as autumn approaches, the sales market is gradually becoming active. Without relief measures to facilitate transportation and sales, legitimate business operations will inevitably come to a standstill, and merchants will suffer losses that are unbearable. We sincerely request that measures be taken to provide relief and facilitate transportation, etc.' While the matter was under review, this association received another letter from the Hankou General Chamber of Commerce, stating that it had received a communication from the Hubei Provincial Government forwarding the Ministry of Finance's Consultation No. 28659, Series Customs, dated July 31, 1936, stating that 'It is permissible that many goods seized by various provinces were purchased before the implementation of the Transportation and Sales Regulations and should not be punished. Various parties have repeatedly telegraphed to request a response from the Ministry. It is now stipulated that "goods purchased by inland businesses before the implementation of the Transportation and Sales Regulations should not be subject to the provisions of the Transportation and Sales Regulations. However, if a large quantity of goods is suspected of being smuggled by Customs, Customs may investigate and handle the matter in accordance with the Anti-Smuggling Regulations," etc., requesting that this association take note and forward the information. The transportation of inventory from various businesses in this city to inland areas is indeed difficult. If no relief measures are provided, the impact will be significant. Based on this regulation, this association drafted a sample inventory certificate, submitted it to the Fourth Standing Committee Meeting of this association for deliberation and approval, and is still awaiting submission to the National Association of Inspection for Smuggling, requesting that the Ministry of Finance approve its implementation, etc.' A record of the proceedings is attached. We hereby attach a sample inventory certificate and submit it to your Association for review, requesting that it be forwarded to the Ministry of Finance for approval and implementation in order to provide relief and facilitate transportation, which would be in the public interest, etc., to the Association. This Association believes that the difficulty in transportation, as stated, is indeed the case. We hereby attach a sample inventory certificate drafted by the Association and submit it for review, requesting that its implementation be approved to facilitate the transportation of goods, which would be in the public interest."

National Assembly Venue to be Equipped with Red and Green Lights; What Chu Minyi Said Upon Arriving in Shanghai

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, Chu Minyi, Deputy Director of the National Assembly Election General Office, arrived in Shanghai by train from Nanjing at approximately 7:00 AM yesterday. He is here to preside over the opening ceremony of the Sino-French National Institute of Technology today and is scheduled to return to Nanjing this morning. Regarding the rumored return of Wang Jingwei, Chairman of the Central Political Council, the reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency specifically visited Chu to inquire about the matter. Chu replied that Wang is still in Czechoslovakia and has no plans to return to China. The various rumors circulating are all untrue. Chu continued to say that there is a new piece of equipment to announce for the National Assembly venue project. Several red and green electric lights will be installed in front of the rostrum, with electric wires connected to each delegate's seat. In the future, when discussing and voting on proposals, there will be no need to raise hands. Delegates can press the electric button at their seats. Green indicates approval, and red indicates opposition. The number of votes for and against will be immediately displayed, and errors can be avoided. The system can also identify who voted in favor and who voted against. Otherwise, counting the hands of thousands of people would be too cumbersome. Furthermore, the stage and music stage are now being expanded to accommodate a hundred or more musicians for ensemble performances. It is planned to invite a Soviet song and dance troupe to China through the China-Soviet Cultural Association, headed by Sun Zhesheng, and they will perform there in the future. Chu also stated that now that the Guangxi issue has been resolved and national unification has been achieved, it is not necessary for Mr. Bai Chongxi to visit Chairman Chiang in Guangdong. It is acceptable for him to meet Chairman Chiang in Nanjing in the future. It is rumored that Bai will form a military inspection delegation to go abroad, which may be true. However, the Central Government hopes that Bai will come to Nanjing as soon as possible.

Printing Industry Association; Reorganizing Association Affairs; Urging Fellow Businesses to Register

The Shanghai Printing Industry Association, in order to implement the central government's promulgated measures to sanction businesses that do not join the association, and fearing that businesses may misunderstand the legal principles and cause confusion, issued a letter on the 14th of this month, urging businesses throughout the city to comply with the association's regulations and printed and distributed the aforementioned measures to inform the public. It also placed advertisements on the front pages of the Shen Bao and Xinwen Bao newspapers on the 16th and 17th of this month, setting a deadline for businesses throughout the city to register with the association by the end of this month. As of yesterday, dozens of businesses, including Cangjie, Nanyang, Wuzhou, Tiantian, Tiancheng, Junyi, and Liguo, have registered. This shows that businesses throughout the city are able to comply with the recently promulgated measures, and the spirit of unity among businesses is consistent. As the registration deadline is fast approaching, those who have not yet registered should do so immediately to achieve a unified organization, so that the association's affairs and business operations can be developed in accordance with regulations. If businesses still fail to register after the deadline, the association will report to the competent authorities for sanctions in accordance with the law. It is hoped that businesses that have not yet joined the association will pay attention.

Business Administration Society; Zhu and Zhao Gave Lectures Yesterday

The Chinese Business Administration Society held a lecture meeting yesterday at the cafeteria of the YMCA of the Eight Immortals Bridge. Zhu Xuefan, the Chinese representative to the International Labour Conference who recently returned to China, was specially invited to give a lecture on the labour conditions in Germany and Italy. Zhao Shu of the General Staff Headquarters of the National Government was also invited to speak on the preparations of the business community during extraordinary times. Attendees included Zhao Yunxiang, chairman of the society; Hu Xiyuan, Ji Jiannan, Pan Yangyao, Shi Jiuyun, and Xiang Kangyuan, executive directors; Cheng Shouzhong, director; and members Ren Shigang, Fang Jiange, and more than forty others. Chairman Cao Yunxiang first reported on the society's affairs, followed by Zhu Xuefan's lecture, the main points of which were that the labour enterprises in Germany and Italy were the most successful among European countries. Not only do workers have trade union organizations, but employers also have trade association organizations. Both labor and management consider it their duty to contribute to national production, and there are few unnecessary disputes. Even if there are disputes, they are easily resolved because their people have received considerable education and have undergone group training since childhood. Therefore, social evil forces cannot easily infiltrate, and disputes do not escalate. The method of resolving disputes is first through negotiations between the two parties. If no result is achieved, the government intervenes to mediate. If mediation fails, the labour court makes a ruling, which has the power to compel both parties to obey. As for the normal times, there is considerable contact between labor and management, such as holding social gatherings. Employers are also very concerned about the welfare of labor, so the relationship is very good and disputes rarely occur. Zhao Shu then spoke on the preparations of the business community during extraordinary times. He first stated the inevitability of a second world war, then the precarious situation of China, and finally said that everyone should be prepared. He believed that the business community had a heavy responsibility and needed to be fully prepared. As for how the business community should prepare, Zhao also gave a description, the main points of which were: (1) actively develop industry, especially heavy industry, such as steel, mining, chemicals, power, and electricity; (2) promote scientific research; (3) concentrate organizations; (4) seek economic self-sufficiency; (5) implement thrift; (6) invest in production enterprises related to national defense.

Report from the Disaster Relief Investigators of the Sino-Foreign Charity Relief Association; Deliberating on the Yellow River Prevention Plan in Western Shandong

Last summer, the levee breached at Dongzhuang on the Yellow River, causing severe disaster in western Shandong. Although the breach has been repaired recently and the floodwaters have returned to the channel, the land is covered with mud and sand, making it unsuitable for cultivation and resulting in a hopeless harvest. The China Sino-Foreign Charity Relief Association, located at No. 505 Henan Road in this city, in order to properly plan for the aftermath, specially dispatched Ji Lu, Director of the Shandong Disaster Relief Investigation; Zhang Chun, Chief Engineer; and Tada, Consulting Engineer, to Jixiang, Lutai, Dongping, and Heze to investigate the post-disaster situation and instructed them to formulate a fundamental Yellow River disaster prevention plan for adoption. Mr. Ji and others were dispatched to go forward, which lasted for two weeks, to visit officials and gentry in various places and solicit opinions. They returned to the Association the day before yesterday to report. The report and plan are summarized as follows: "We, Lu and others, previously received the Association's order to investigate the current situation after the disaster in western Shandong and to plan for the fundamental Yellow River disaster prevention. Starting from Linpu, we traveled southeast to Yutai, turned north through Jixiang and Yuncheng, and then northeast to Dongping. Then, along the west bank of the Grand Canal, we crossed Jining and returned. We traveled through ten counties for two weeks. Along the way, the land was barren, the people were emaciated, and the broken walls and ruins were heartbreaking. The severity of the disaster and the hardship of life were evident without investigation. What is lamentable is that the farmers have lost or sold all their livestock and have no way to cultivate the land. Every household or several households work together to pull a plow to replace the oxen. However, the mud and sand brought by the Yellow River have accumulated everywhere, shallow at an inch or so, deep at several feet, with a solid and greasy texture, making it difficult to apply force. Even those who have sown seeds and seedlings are subject to corrosion by black insects and hindered by waterlogging, making it difficult to expect a harvest. The fear of food shortages in the future can be foreseen. As for the fundamental Yellow River disaster prevention methods, as far as we can see, local disaster victims can be mobilized to carry out relief efforts and complete the following two projects: (1) Dredge the Zhao Wang and Wanfu Rivers to allow the Yellow River to be diverted to Nanyang Dushan and other lakes to facilitate drainage; (2) Build a long levee from the Grand Canal along the Songjin River and the upper reaches of the Zhao Wang River to the Henan border and the south bank of the Yellow River, and build a floodgate at the southern end of the levee and several sluice gates at the northern end, each equipped with control mechanisms. When the Yellow River rises sharply, the floodgate will automatically open, and part of the water will be diverted to the Zhao Wang and Wanfu Rivers, etc., to the Nanyang and other lakes. The remaining water will return to the Yellow River through the Songjin River and the western section of the Grand Canal. In this way, the floodwaters will be diverted and the tragic disaster of flooding can be avoided again. Whether the plan for preventing the Yellow River disaster in western Shandong is appropriate is respectfully submitted for consideration and implementation."

Tea Industry Representatives Petitioning to Return to Shanghai; Reported on the Process Yesterday; Decided to Organize a Unified Export Tea Market; Ministry of Industry Needs to Study This

According to the Shen Shi News Agency, the Foreign Firms Tea Industry Association of this city, in order to concentrate its strength, develop foreign trade, and restore the reputation of Chinese tea internationally, convened a general meeting of all members this month to discuss the measures. The members unanimously agreed that in order to revitalize the export of tea leaves, it is necessary to unite the industry as a prerequisite. On the 17th, Ye Shichang, chairman of the association; Sun Zifu, supervisor; and Yu Daxiong and Cao Yunjie, consultants, took the draft articles of association to Nanjing to petition the Ministry of Industry. They returned to Shanghai by train on the night of the 19th and convened a general meeting of all members at the association's address in Gujia Lane at 1:00 PM yesterday. Representatives from fourteen tea firms, including Zhongxin Chang, Yongxinglong, Hongyuanyong, Yuanfengrun, Shengchangsheng, Dashengyong, Rendeyong, Yilong, Shenyuan, Xietai, Tongtai, Xielong, Yitai, and Zhenhe, attended.

National Products Manufacturers Association Requests External Negotiations on Vietnamese Tax Rates, Striving for Equality to Strengthen Friendship

The Shanghai Chinese National Products Manufacturers Association yesterday submitted a petition to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs stating that it was requesting negotiations with the Vietnamese government to lower tax rates and ensure equal treatment to benefit the production and sales of domestic goods. The petition stated that the Shanghai office of the Vietnam Chinese National Products Company had sent a letter stating (excerpt) that the Vietnamese government has been specifically raising tax rates on popular Chinese goods imported into Vietnam. For example, canned food, as mentioned in the previous letter, initially had a tax of 12.5 Vietnamese dollars per 100 kilograms of gross weight, but recently this has increased to 58 Vietnamese dollars per 100 kilograms, equivalent to 160 national currency dollars. There are many such examples. According to the Association, this measure by the Vietnamese government obviously disregards national friendship and hinders the promotion of Chinese goods in Vietnam, which contradicts Article 2 of the Sino-French Customs Treaty, which stipulates that "neither of the contracting countries shall, under any pretext, impose on goods transported and imported by the people of the other contracting country, within their own territories, dependencies, colonies, and protectorates, customs duties, inland taxes, or any taxes higher than or different from those paid by their own people or the people of any other country." It is requested that your ministry strictly negotiate with the Vietnamese government to ensure that all goods are taxed equally, in order to strengthen friendship and benefit the export of national goods. This is eagerly awaited. Advisors Yu Daxiong and Cao Yunjie, among others, were present. Chairman Ye Shichang reported that during this trip to Beijing to petition, Wu Dingchang, the actual director, had gone to Zhenjiang to attend the establishment of the National Economic Cooperation Association Zhenjiang Branch. Zhou Yichun, the deputy director, received them and stated that the plan to organize the export tea market (including black and green tea) still needs to be studied further, and a reply will be given in two weeks.

China Cotton Company Leases Hengfeng Yarn Factory, Commencing Operations Today; Hu Yungan to Concurrently Serve as Factory Manager; Hiring of Veteran Workers to Initially Open Regular Day Shifts

The China Cotton Trading Company, recognizing this year's abundant cotton harvest in China, has allocated significant funds to purchase new cotton from various regions. Simultaneously, it has leased the Hengfeng Textile Factory for its own spinning and weaving operations. After signing a three-year lease agreement with Nie Lusheng, the factory manager, the company has completed the preparation of the factory's machinery. Hu Yungan, the general manager of the company, will concurrently serve as the factory manager, with someone surnamed Zai from Fuli appointed as the factory's assistant and chief engineer. Veteran management personnel from the coarse and fine yarn departments and the weaving department have been retained. However, the heads of each department will be reassigned. Trial runs have been conducted for several days, and the factory is scheduled to officially commence operations today. The hired workers are all former veteran workers, and initially, only regular day shifts will be operated. Night shifts will be added as needed. The factory has 54,916 spindles and 611 looms. It will use 153,045 dan of cotton to produce 43,250 bales of yarn and 20,719,500 square yards of cloth. It is said that this factory was the first yarn factory established in China. There will be magic shows by Xu Suzhen and Zhang Zhen, and a one-act play performed by female stars from the Mingxing Film Company, led by Ms. Hu Die, titled "She Ying Chang" (Photography Studio), "Jie Tou Xiang Wei" (Streets and Alleys), and "Qiu Hun" (Marriage Proposal). The Peking opera performances will include "Zhuo Fang Cao" (Catching and Releasing Cao) and "Xin Wu Hua Dong" (New Five Flower Cave). Finally, all the male and female stars will perform "Qun Xing Xian Ji" (All-Star Machine Offering), with each act being wonderful and a once-in-a-lifetime grand event. It is hoped that all sectors will actively participate and contribute to the grand occasion.

Two Reefs Discovered in Xishan Bay

Notice No. 217 from the Hydrographic Office of the Naval Department reads: "Two reefs have been discovered in the anchorage of Xishan Bay on the southeast coast of China. One (1) is located at 6 degrees from the summit of Xishan's 282 peak, at a distance of 2 chains (each chain is equal to 1 nautical mile), at 117 degrees 4 minutes East longitude and 23 degrees 35 minutes North latitude. The current state is that the reef is exposed 2 feet above the water surface (i.e., 0.61 meters). A danger line should be drawn around the symbol of the exposed reef, with the note 'Dry 2 feet.' The other (2) is located at 39 degrees from the summit of Xishan's 282 peak, at a distance of 2.65 chains. The current state is that the reef is exposed 6 feet above the water surface (1.83 meters). A danger line should be drawn around the symbol of the exposed reef, with the note 'Dry 6 feet.' This was discovered by the customs patrol ship Dexing and has been notified to all maritime transports."

Autumn Cocoons from Jiangsu and Zhejiang Enter the Market; Cocoon Merchants Begin Purchasing; Zhejiang Control Association Issues Notice to Prevent Price Gouging, Conducting Separate Inspections After Drying

Autumn cocoons from Jiangsu and Zhejiang have entered the market, and cocoon merchants have successively started purchasing. All purchases are being made in accordance with the standard prices stipulated by the National Economic Council's Sericulture Improvement Committee. The Zhejiang Silk Control Association has issued a notice to prevent price gouging, conducting separate inspections after drying. Details are as follows:

Autumn Cocoons Enter the Market; Cocoon Merchants Begin Purchasing

The silk control organizations in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces will continue to control this year's autumn cocoons as usual. All silk manufacturers and remaining cocoon merchants who wish to purchase autumn cocoons must register with the control organization. Only after passing the review will they be allowed to purchase. Currently, autumn cocoons in areas such as Haining, Jiaxing, Chongde, and Pinghu in Zhejiang, and Wuxi and Liyang in Jiangsu have successively entered the market. All registered and qualified manufacturers have borrowed funds from banks or money houses and started purchasing. Due to the yellowing of mulberry leaves this autumn in both provinces, the harvest is not as good as the spring cocoons. According to estimates by the control organizations, the total output will be 400,000 dan of fresh cocoons. The opening dates for cocoon merchants in various places are longer than for spring cocoons, totaling about seven days.

Preventing Malpractices; Separate Inspection

The Zhejiang Silk Control Committee announced that the standard price for this year's autumn cocoons has been approved by the Zhejiang Provincial Government and is calculated based on the size of the reeling ratio. For example, if the reeling ratio is 460 catties, the price of fresh cocoons is 29 yuan per market dan. If the reeling ratio is 430 catties, the price is 32 yuan. If the reeling ratio is 500 catties, the price is 26 yuan. The price is proportionally calculated for reeling ratios between 430 catties and 500 catties. Prices can also be proportionally adjusted for those less than 430 catties or more than 500 catties. However, it is believed that there will be very few improved varieties with reeling ratios exceeding 500 catties. To prevent price gouging, cocoon merchants who purchase fresh cocoons with reeling ratios less than 430 catties or more than 500 catties should store them separately and wait for inspection and release. All cocoon merchants in various counties and cities are required to comply. Anyone who dares to violate this will be punished in accordance with Article 16 of the Provisional Measures for the Control and Management of Cocoon Purchasing. This notice is hereby issued.

Shanghai South Second Route Public Buses Began Operation Yesterday

The city-run public bus system inaugurated the Second Route Caohejing Line yesterday. Buses will run from 6:00 AM to 9:00 PM, every twelve minutes. Because the seats are comfortable and the fares are low, passengers are happy to ride. According to the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities, this line will be an important east-west transportation artery in Nanshi. The line runs from the emerging town of Caohejing, through Xujiahui, the new western district, and the densely populated urban and rural areas, to reach the Sixteenth Pier. Xujiahui and the nearby Tushanwan are the center of Catholicism in Shanghai and have a large population. Previously, they relied entirely on the French Concession's Second Route tram and the Nian'er Route public bus for transportation. Now, they can reach the Pudong waterfront via a shorter route. The new western district was formerly the political center of the city and has been developed for twenty years. After the municipal government moved, it is now the location of the municipal party headquarters. In the past five years, the number of residents in the area has gradually increased. In the future, after the establishment of Zhongshan Hospital and the National Medical College, there will be even more hope for development. Therefore, the opening of this route has a significant effect on transportation in the city.

Elementary School Student Climbs Ceiling, Dies Tragically After Falling

Fei Jiasheng, a 42-year-old from Huzhou who works at the China Merchants Bureau and resides at 144 Mintiniyin Road in the French Concession, had only one son named Yulin, who was 12 years old this year and studying at the Sino-French School. At 5:00 PM on the 19th, after returning home from night school, he climbed onto the glass ceiling of the atrium from the window of the three-story building to play. He accidentally stepped on the glass, causing it to break, and fell from a height, suffering head and brain injuries and losing consciousness. He was sent to Guangci Hospital, but died due to the severity of his injuries before he could be treated. The hospital reported the incident to the French police station, which sent detectives to investigate. The body was transported to the Tongren Fuyuan sub-hall for examination, and a request will be made to the Special Second Court for an autopsy today.

Teenager Commits Suicide by Poisoning After Failing陆大 Entrance Exam; Discords with Family Over Education; Feng Zhibo in Dilemma, Disgusted with the World

The Yangtze Hotel at the intersection of Hankou Road and Yunnan Road had a guest check in on the evening of the 7th of this month, stating that he wanted to rent a room. Room 608 was assigned to him. He claimed to be named Zhang Wenzhang, from Haining, and was 23 years old. He seemed peaceful and calm. Until yesterday morning around 10 o'clock, when the tea boy entered the room to clean, he suddenly noticed a pungent medicinal smell. He found Zhang Wenzhang lying in bed, unconscious, with a half-empty bottle of some kind of liquid medicine beside his pillow. Realizing that something was wrong, he rushed to the front desk to report it, and the police were notified. They immediately sent a car to rush him to Renji Hospital for treatment. However, as he was unable to speak, the truth was unclear. Later, after an investigation by the Old Gate Police Station, it was discovered that the teenager's real name was Feng Zhibo, 18 years old, from Haiyan, Zhejiang. He had come to Shanghai from his hometown on the 7th of this month. He had studied at Fudan University last semester, and this semester he planned to transfer to the Central Military Academy, but his parents had prevented him. As a result, there was discord between the family over the issue of schooling. Feng, being young and impulsive, angrily ran away from home and came to Shanghai to stay at the Yangtze Hotel, still planning to take the military school entrance exam. However, he was running out of money, and he was in a dilemma, so he resorted to this course of action. It is reported that his condition is still critical.

Jianghai Customs Stipulates Rules for Tugboats and Towed Vessels in the Harbor; Avoiding Navigation Dangers; Ensuring Civil Aviation Safety

T.H. Behre, the harbor master of the Jianghai Customs, issued Notice No. 15 to stipulate the rules for the operation of tugboats and towed vessels within the port. The notice stated that "The number of vessels navigating within the port of this harbor is increasing, and the number of large and small ships and civilian ships transporting goods is also increasing from time to time. Now, in order to find ways to avoid navigation dangers and protect the safety of life on various civilian ships, special rules are stipulated for the operation of tugboats and towed vessels within the port limits as follows: (1) Iron barges, (A) those with a capacity of 100 tons and below, each tugboat may tow up to three barges, with one barge alongside the tugboat and two barges in a row attached to the tugboat. (B) Those with a capacity of more than 100 tons, each tugboat may tow up to two barges, attached alongside the tugboat. (2) Sailing boats, (A) the number of sailing boats towed by a tugboat shall not exceed two at a time and shall be attached alongside the tugboat. (B) If a tugboat tows a Fuzhou wooden boat, only one boat shall be attached alongside the tugboat at a time. (3) Passenger boats and cargo boats, a tugboat shall not tow more than six boats at a time, with two boats side by side in each row, for a total of three rows attached to the tugboat. (4) Fishing boats and garbage boats, a tugboat shall not tow more than nine boats at a time, with three boats side by side in each row, for a total of three rows attached to the tugboat. (5) Rafts, a tugboat shall only be allowed to tow one row at a time, and the length and width limits are as follows: (A) Between Wusong and Donggou, the length shall not exceed 70.2 meters (250 feet) and the width shall not exceed 15.2 meters (50 feet). (B) Between Donggou and the floating pontoon above the Jiangnan Shipyard, the length shall not exceed 45.7 meters (150 feet) and the width shall not exceed 9.2 meters (30 feet). (C) Above the floating pontoon of the Jiangnan Shipyard, the length shall not exceed 122 meters (400 feet) and the width shall not exceed 30.5 meters (100 feet). All rafts within the above-mentioned three sections of this harbor must travel close to the shallow water and must completely avoid the waterways used by transport ships. All tugboats must comply with Article 19 of the Shanghai Harbor Management Ship Regulations and have sufficient control over the various types of vessels being towed. All shipowners are required to be aware of this notice."

Gunfire at Yaojia Stone Bridge in Zhabei at Night; Four Bandits Opened Fire to Resist Arrest; One Thief Eventually Arrested

At around 8:30 PM last night, four bandits suddenly appeared at Yaojia Stone Bridge in Zhabei, attempting to rob the property of a local family. A patrolling police officer happened to pass by and, finding their actions suspicious, attempted to search them. The four bandits immediately opened fire to resist. The police officer returned fire, but none of the shots hit. Three bandits then escaped into the darkness. One bandit, Wu Xianfu, from Dongtai, age 35, was arrested at the scene. A wooden fake handgun was found on him. He was taken into custody for interrogation. Wu confessed that he, along with his accomplices Yang Huibiao, Zhang Xingfa, Wen Gui, and Enfu (who are still at large), had robbed the Wansen Sauce Garden on Shajing Road and the No. 932 Tobacco Shop at the end of Tianbao Road on the 26th day of the seventh lunar month. They divided the stolen goods and spent them. The police station has sent Wu, along with the fake gun, to the police station for interrogation. The remaining accomplices who are at large will be arrested and punished in due course.

Remains in a Box Near Qu Zhenren Road; Skeleton-like Remains; Difficult to Determine if Death was Due to Illness or Murder; Remains Sent to Zhenru for Examination

Near Xieqiao Qu Zhenren Road, a wooden box was discovered two days ago. Upon inspection, a corpse was found inside, with suspicious traces. The local police station instructed the local security guard, Gu Xueyuan, to report to the local court for inspection. Prosecutor Kong and investigator Shen were appointed to the scene. The investigation revealed that the corpse had already rotted and was almost a skeleton, making it difficult to determine the gender or whether the death was due to illness or murder. Therefore, yesterday, it was ordered that the remains be transported by car to the Zhenru Forensic Research Institute for detailed examination. At the same time, the local security guard was instructed to investigate whether the deceased had any family members for further verification, forwarding them to our association for compilation and transfer. This is what we hope for.

At 5:10 PM on the 19th, a Hubin Company bus from Minhang to Shanghai at 5:00 suddenly encountered three female Girl Scouts from Shanghai County Middle School riding bicycles as it approached the North Bridge Station. Sailing Boat Robbed by Pirates

Zhang Shengqiao, a resident of Pudong, owns a sailing boat that carries passengers and goods between Wuku and Shanghai. The other day, he loaded 134 piculs of white rice from the Shenchang Rice Shop, 30 piculs of white rice from the Qianfeng Rice Shop, and three pieces of tung oil returned by the Qia Taiyi to the Yuanfeng Tung Oil Company at Wuku in the morning and set sail for Shanghai. After sailing to Minhang, he stopped briefly to wait for the tide. He continued sailing at 1 PM. Unexpectedly, when he reached the vicinity of a link between rivers at Yilintang, at around 9 PM at dusk, a small boat blocked his path. Two people standing on the bow of the small boat raised guns and ordered him to stop. The boatmen knew it was a robbery, but under duress, they had to lower the sails and comply. First, two people jumped on board. Then, six bandits with a Hubei accent, all dressed in short clothes, climbed aboard and dropped anchor chains. They immediately began to rob. First, they searched all the boatmen, but found nothing. Then, they put the boatmen in the stern cabin. There were two passengers. In addition to losing all their cash of eight dollars and seventy cents, all their luggage, bedding, rattan boxes, etc., were looted. Before fleeing, they moved six piculs of white rice (including 5.5 piculs under the name of Shenchang Company and 0.5 piculs under the name of Qianfeng Company) and three pieces of tung oil onto their boat and sailed away. Because it was late at night, there were no boats passing by, so no one could hear the calls for help. They had to let them load up and leave. Upon arriving in Shanghai, they reported to the Water Police Bureau and asked them to investigate. It is said that the loss from this robbery was not small, amounting to two or three hundred yuan. Fortunately, no one was injured, which was the great fortune among misfortune.

Two Clubs Fight; Three Shot and Injured; Truth Unknown; Three Detained, One Released

At around 9 PM on the 8th of this month, members of the Tongqunle and Xinshenghuo clubs on Renzhili, North Sichuan Road, had a major brawl for unknown reasons. As a result, the Xinshenghuo side lost. Cantonese individuals Yi Qibin, Wang Zhuan, and Hu Kang were shot and wounded in their hands, legs, and abdomens. They were taken to Tongren Hospital for treatment. The Hongkou Police Department dispatched Chinese and Western detectives to investigate and found that Liang Dagang, Xi Yao, and Zhang Wen, three Cantonese employees of the Guanzhen Restaurant at No. 401 Wuchang Road, were involved in the fight. They were detained and sent to the First Special District Court. The victims had not yet arrived, so they were temporarily detained. Yesterday, Judge Zhong Qing questioned them in the Criminal Division Three. Zhang Wen, one of the suspects, was found to be unrelated and was released. Zhang Shizhu, the lawyer for the Public Works Department, stated that the victim Yi Qibin had not yet recovered and was still in the hospital for treatment. Wang Zhuan and Hu Kang were in court to testify. According to Chinese Constable No. 1155, when he arrived at the scene, he saw thirty to forty people fighting each other. After a while, they dispersed in different directions. He did not hear any gunshots. He did not see the two defendants at the scene. Witness Chen Qian stated that the defendant Liang Dagang was holding a handgun at the time. The victim Wang Zhuan stated that he was cut in the leg by Liang Dagang with a knife and heard gunshots. Hu Kang stated that his right wrist was hit by a stray bullet. He did not see who fired it. When questioned, the two defendants firmly denied participating in the fight. The defense lawyer, Wu Zhenming, stated that the Tongqunle and Xinshenghuo clubs were formal business meeting places, not gatherings of thugs. The two defendants were mistakenly detained and asked the court to consider this. Judge Zhong ordered that they be remanded and rescheduled for verification.

Public Security Bureau Issues Notice on Railway Warning Signs to Prevent Danger

Cai Jingjun, the director of the Shanghai Public Security Bureau, issued a notice yesterday stating, "I have received Municipal Government Order No. 20150, which states, 'I have received Official Letter No. 2142 from the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration, which states, "Warning signs have been erected at level crossings and bridges along the railway to alert pedestrians and avoid danger. However, pedestrians passing over the tracks either do not pay attention or do not understand the meaning of these warning signs, resulting in frequent injuries and deaths. In addition to further improving these warning signs to make them more visible, and strictly instructing drivers to pay close attention, we plan to ask your government to issue a notice to all townships and towns near the railway tracks, instructing the public to pay attention to the warning signs when approaching the tracks in order to ensure their safety through vigilance. This is of great benefit. We hereby request your approval and response. In light of this, the matter concerns alerting pedestrians and avoiding danger, and should be handled accordingly. In addition to responding to the official letter, the bureau is instructed to immediately comply, issue a notice to inform the public near the railway, etc." In light of this, in addition to instructing subordinates to provide guidance and correction at any time, a notice is hereby issued, urging all citizens to pay attention."

Copper and Tin Trade Association Encourages Colleagues to Join

The Shanghai Copper and Tin Trade Association at No. 1079 Lujiabang Road, Nanshi, Shanghai, has found that less than half of the colleagues in Nanshi have joined the association. To comply with the revised Measures for Sanctioning Companies and Firms that do not Join Associations issued by the Central Training Department, the association has notified and urged colleagues who have not yet joined to join quickly. The original notice is recorded as follows: "It is hereby noted that Article 2 of the revised Measures for Sanctioning Companies and Firms that do not Join Associations issued by the Central Training Department states, 'Commercial firms that have not joined a trade association shall be formally required by the trade association to join within a specified period. If they fail to comply within the specified period, the trade association may investigate and present the matter to the competent authorities for sanctions in accordance with the revised sanctioning measures, and order them to suspend operations, etc.' In light of this, it is noted that there are many commercial firms in this city engaged in the copper and tungsten industry, but less than half have joined the association. In order to unite colleagues and maintain the law, this association, with the intention of advising before punishing, again urges all colleagues in the city who have not yet joined to join the association within the specified period. Do not hesitate any longer and violate the law, which may lead to inconvenience."

Pig Industry Seeks Solution to Overdue Accounts

The Shanghai Pig Industry Trade Association, in view of the fact that in the past year, due to market conditions, business has been slow for various meat shops, resulting in overdue accounts totaling more than one million yuan, which is almost unsustainable for those with weaker capital, recently proposed to convene all members to reorganize the industry regulations to remedy the situation. A notice was sent to all members, stating that the decline of our industry in recent years is becoming more and more serious. The reason for the failure is that the credit sales have been too excessive and unlimited. In order to easily sell goods, we do not ask whether the accounts can be collected. We have greatly expanded our sales, so although the doors are like a market, we are actually strong on the outside but weak on the inside. When it comes to paying the accounts, it is inevitable that there will be delays. If we do not take immediate action to recover, every family will go bankrupt. I hope that all members will be concerned about their own interests and the overall situation of the whole body, and I hope that everyone will express their opinions and discuss the process.

Killer in Shipmate Murder Case Apprehended Yesterday

Around 8 AM on the 15th of this month, near the entrance of the Fuxin First Flour Mill on Guangfu Road (west of the Xinza Bridge) in Zhabei, over ten dockworkers were unloading flour from a ship when a rice boat shipmate named He San'nan returned from buying vegetables. He yielded to a car and a handcart, causing them to collide with a dockworker, and two bags of flour to fall. The shipmate was then beaten to death by the dockworkers. The Xinza Branch Bureau dispatched police officers to the scene, and took foreman Gao Yujie, witness Chen Qifu (a leather worker), and dockworkers Bian Yubao, Zu Yechang, and others, a total of ten people, to the bureau. Meanwhile, local guarantor Shen Xiaowu was instructed to report to the Shanghai Local Court. Around 4 PM, Prosecutor Tang Ruxiu arrived for an examination and determined that the deceased He San'nan had indeed been beaten to death, with two front teeth knocked out and fatal injuries to the chest and other parts of the body. The local guarantor was instructed to have the deceased's brother, He Shengda, make arrangements for the burial. The police bureau was instructed to bring the culprit to justice for interrogation. However, after the incident, the culprit, feeling guilty, immediately fled, so the foreman Gao Yujie and the other ten, who had already been apprehended, were sent to the court. Unexpectedly, around 11 AM yesterday, the Xinza Branch Bureau received a phone call from the Yangjiadu Police Station in Pudong, reporting that the culprit in the case had been apprehended by the station. Chief Liao of the Zhabei branch bureau immediately dispatched detectives Bao and Qian, along with squad leader Li Shoushen and detectives Zhao Chunsen and Sun Youzhi, carrying official documents, and brought him back around 5 PM. The suspect was identified as Zhao Hongke, 32 years old, from Huaicheng, residing at No. 213 Yaoshi Lane, Xiaoshadu. He previously worked as a laborer at the Huafeng Factory. He confessed without hesitation to killing the shipmate, saying that even if he had not been apprehended, he would have voluntarily surrendered to avoid implicating his many companions. He claimed to have had an old feud with the deceased. He stated that he has a grandmother and mother, Ms. Wang, and a wife and two daughters in his hometown, all dependent on him, and no brothers.

Introducing Two Recent Works by Wang Yuanzhong

Mr. Wang Yuanzhong, a professor in the Faculty of Arts and the head of the Department of Chinese Language at Daxia University, is deeply learned and has written extensively. Recently, he has published two works, "Essential Points of the Hundred Schools of Thought" and "A Chronicle of Yan Fu," published by the Zhonghua Book Company and the Commercial Press. The "Essential Points" is an exegesis of thirteen articles on schools of thought since the Zhou, Qin, and Han dynasties, covering the various schools and the essentials of academic fire. It is no less than a new path for those studying philosophy. Liang Qichao and Sun Deqian have praised it highly. Appended is a questionnaire on the extant books of the various schools, listing the advantages and disadvantages of various editions, as well as the annotations, collected works, and lost works of the various schools, making it convenient for scholars. The "Chronicle of Yan Fu" systematically describes the life of Yan Fu, who was the first to introduce Western culture and scholarship to China. The chronicle provides detailed accounts of his introductions and his views on politics and scholarship, drawing on forty to fifty books and visiting dozens of his descendants and relatives. The thoroughness is evident. The above two books are highly relevant to both new and old scholarship, and those interested in national studies should have a copy. It is said that sales are unusually brisk and that a reprint is forthcoming.

Statistics on Criminal Cases in the City Last Week

The Municipal Public Security Bureau released yesterday statistics on criminal cases occurring within the city limits from September 11th to 17th, totaling 258 cases, with 433 male and female suspects arrested. A breakdown follows: Robbery and aggravated robbery, 18 cases, 33 suspects; Rape and abduction, 33 cases, 50 suspects; Gambling, 7 cases, 45 suspects; Fraud, 18 cases, 97 suspects; Communist Party cases, 1 case, 2 suspects; Homicide, 5 cases, 18 suspects; Arson, 3 cases, 3 suspects; Counterfeiting, 3 cases, 4 suspects; Violations of police regulations, 17 cases, 22 suspects; Other criminal cases, 4 cases, 64 suspects. Total: 258 cases, 433 suspects. All suspects arrested have undergone preliminary investigation by the Third Section. Apart from 114 cases, in which the crimes were minor and were handled according to regulations on violations of police laws, or those who were released after sentencing, the remaining suspects have been transferred to the local court or other competent authorities for trial. The number of criminal cases and suspects arrested this week decreased by 49 and 154 respectively compared to last week.

The store announced to customers that the department would be temporarily closed for several hours and immediately began repairs. Letter to the Editor

Yesterday, I read a news item in your newspaper about a motorcycle falling into the river on the Shanghai-Minhang Road, claiming that "I am a tax inspector stationed in Shanghai by the Finance Bureau, and on the 18th, I was driving a motorcycle on the Shanghai-Minhang South Zhejiang Road line in the Liangmiao area in western Shanghai. Because I was driving too far, both I and the motorcycle fell into the river. I was seriously injured and unable to get up. Later, I was sent to the Guangci Hospital for treatment." This is not in accordance with the facts. Now I will inform you of the details and request a correction. I work for a manufacturer and have never worked for the Finance Bureau or any other agency. On that day, I was driving to Hangzhou for sightseeing. When passing through Qianliangmiao, I was overturned due to unevenness. Fortunately, only my arm was slightly scratched and I was not injured in the waist or legs. I returned to Shanghai from Minhang and was not treated at Guangci Hospital. I believe that it was a false rumor that caused my relatives and friends to inquire after me. I am very grateful and hope for a correction. Respectfully, Liu Shunchang, September 20th, No. 2171, Xujiahui Xietu Road.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated: The weather around Shandong is volatile and unstable, with cyclones caused by the passage of a small low-pressure system moving eastward. The Yellow River basin is sunny, with some cloud cover and strong northwest winds. The upper and middle reaches of the Yangtze River have southwest winds, and the lower reaches of the Yangtze River have southeast winds. The weather in the East China Sea and Taiwan will change from cloudy to overcast, with strong northeast winds. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the temperature in this city reached a high of 86.4 degrees and a low of 59.0 degrees. On the same day last year, the high was 83.1 degrees and the low was 60.3 degrees.

Education News

Jiangsu Province's Education Expenditure for the Past Three Years: Funding Increases Annually, with Compulsory Education Receiving the Most

Jiangsu Province's educational expenditure has been streamlined in recent years, and attention has been paid to its sources, resulting in a more stable foundation and an increase in the amount of funding each year. The total expenditure on education in the 22nd year of the Republic was 4,446,884 yuan, accounting for 20.198% of the province's total expenditure. The total expenditure on education in the 23rd year was 4,446,568 yuan, accounting for 16.76% of the province's total expenditure. The total expenditure on education in the 24th year was 4,578,028 yuan, accounting for 15.86% of the province's total expenditure. The budget for the province's educational expenditure for the 25th year has also been compiled and submitted to the provincial government for review by the central government. The total expenditure listed is 5,736,280 yuan, an increase of 1,157,252 yuan compared to the 24th year (the actual expenditure now is less than this number). The largest increase is in funding for compulsory education and vocational schools. The increase in funding for vocational schools is significant, accounting for more than 32% of the funding for secondary schools, which is not far from the Ministry's requirement of 35%. The allocation of various educational funds in the province in recent years has also been carried out in strict accordance with the standards promulgated by the Ministry. The percentages are as follows:

Type of Expenditure 22nd Year 23rd Year 24th Year

Higher Education 4.28 5.64 7.65

Secondary Education 52.41 54.42 55.11

Primary Education 9.47 9.61 9.02

Social Education 15.11 15.68 16.21

Educational Administration 6.91 6.87 6.96

Other Expenses 11.82 7.78 5.05

Furthermore, the province's allocation of secondary education funding has been improved year by year in accordance with the regulations of the Ministry, and it is expected that the Ministry's standard will be reached by the prescribed deadline (26th year). The percentage of secondary education funding allocation for the past three years is recorded below:

Category Ministry Standard 22nd Year 23rd Year 24th Year

General Middle School 40.00 49.80 46.58 46.63

Normal School 25.00 30.93 28.11 16.08

Vocational School 35.00 19.27 25.31 27.29

Problems in High School Mathematics, Physics, and Chemistry Teaching

The Education College of Central University is Addressing the Problem - Designated as the Central Task for This Year

As previously reported in this newspaper, the experiments and tests conducted by the Education Research Institute of the Education College of Central University on the problem of English teaching in middle schools have concluded, and a detailed report will be published soon. It is now known that the central task of the institute for this year is the "Problem of High School Mathematics, Physics, and Chemistry Teaching." At a time when the government's university policy is shifting towards science and engineering, the question of how to assess and improve the mathematics, physics, and chemistry levels of high school students, and how to effectively improve teaching methods, is extremely important. However, without applying experimental methods for precise empirical research, it is not easy to find solutions. But this type of testing has not yet been tried in our country, and the problem of high school mathematics, physics, and chemistry teaching may become even more serious. The Education College of Central University has expanded based on the education departments of Southeast University and Nanjing Higher Normal School, and its talent and equipment have improved year by year. It has long been known for its expertise in testing. Its efforts in recent years have been highly praised. Furthermore, Central University's science and engineering colleges have developed rapidly in the past four years, and more and more experts in mathematics, physics, and chemistry have been recruited. The college can utilize the talent and equipment of other colleges on the one hand, and closely cooperate with experimental schools on the other, so that experienced high school science teachers can participate, and multiple psychologists, testing, and statistics experts from the college can oversee the completion. Once the testing is completed, the contribution will be significant. All plans have been decided, but funding is still being sought.

Shanghai Social Bureau Calls Meeting with Teachers of Silk Factory Literacy Classes

Director Pan Delivers Encouraging Speech; Factory Literacy Classes Begin Today

The literacy classes for silk factory workers are approved to begin today. The Social Bureau has completed the registration of literacy teachers, with a total of 873 qualified teachers. They were summoned to a meeting yesterday morning at 8 AM, presided over by Section Chief Xu Yefu of the Third Section. After the formal greetings, the chairman first reported on the significance of conducting literacy classes for workers and the purpose of convening the meeting. Director Pan Gongzhan then delivered a speech, stating that every citizen should have (1) physical strength, (2) intelligence, and (3) morality, and should concentrate and unite to fulfill the duties of a citizen. The government's purpose in conducting literacy education for workers is to provide literacy education to illiterate people and to teach them civic knowledge, so that in addition to becoming literate, they understand how to be a good person. Everyone should understand their own tasks and the importance of their responsibilities. After individual interviews, qualified individuals were assigned as teachers to various factories. However, China's industry is backward, and under the current economic depression, we must strive to revitalize. Economic construction requires cooperation between labor and management. Class warfare and conflicts between labor and management are suicidal policies that China does not need. Taking silk factories as an example, the situation was good ten years ago, but in recent years, due to the decline of the silk industry, the situation is extremely bad. Factories start work after new cocoons come on the market and stop after the Mid-Autumn Festival. Although this year is slightly better than last year, it cannot be said for certain that it can last through the year. Workers in operating factories have food to eat, while workers in closed factories have no food to eat. Therefore, anyone who violates the Three Principles of the People or slanders the Party and the state will be severely punished. Everyone is serving the country and the nation, sacrificing time and energy, and undertaking arduous work, which is greatly admired. After workers receive literacy education, they can be responsible, trustworthy, and have a sense of honor and shame, so that the nation can be revived. Everyone should understand that they are serving the country, not just doing a job. Serving as a literacy teacher is the same as serving as a member of the defense corps. What is admired is those who are willing to take responsibility. Li Wanqing then gave guidance on teaching, and Wang Gang gave guidance on administration. Finally, individual group discussions were held, and the meeting adjourned at 11 AM.

Overview of Japanese Schools in Shanghai (2)

— Special Report by This Newspaper, Investigation by Hu Zuyin

2. School Buildings and Facilities

There are a total of six Japanese school buildings in Shanghai; because the school building for the Industrial Youth School is attached inside the Northern Japanese Ordinary Elementary School building. The architectural area and the number of classrooms in each school building are different. Now, the investigation of the architectural situation of each school building is copied as follows:

Architectural Overview Table of Japanese School Buildings in Shanghai

Note: One ping equals thirty-six square feet

The types and number of special classrooms in each school vary slightly. Now, the special classrooms of the Central Ordinary Elementary School are listed separately, so that one can see a glimpse of them. The school has seven special classrooms: one craft classroom, one science classroom, one etiquette classroom, one sewing classroom, one drawing classroom, and two singing classrooms. Other rooms include: craft room preparation room, craft materials room, science preparation room, specimen hanging picture room, hygiene room, staff library, children's reading room, martial arts equipment room, sports equipment room, bathroom, reception room, etc.

The Japanese Girls' High School also has one large Chinese, Japanese, and Western cooking experiment room, two tea ceremony practice rooms, one Western-style and one Japanese-style etiquette room, and one dyeing practice room. A new swimming pool was built last year and opened during the summer for male and female students from all Japanese schools in Shanghai to practice swimming. Recently, the Central Ordinary Elementary School is also building a swimming pool for elementary school children to practice swimming.

3. Administrative Facilities

As mentioned in the previous section, the Japanese schools in Shanghai are established by the Shanghai Japanese Residents' Association, so the management rights of each school are in the hands of the cadres of the Residents' Association. The head of the Residents' Association is nominally responsible for managing the schools, but in practice, it is managed by the School Affairs Committee. The members of the School Affairs Committee are appointed by the head of the Residents' Association and are responsible to the head. The planning and management of the construction of school buildings and the allocation of funds are carried out by the School Affairs Committee.

The recruitment of teachers and staff in each school is done by the Japanese Ministry of Education (i.e., the Ministry of Education), which introduces candidates to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs (i.e., the Ministry of Foreign Affairs). The Ministry of Foreign Affairs submits the list of candidates to the Consul-General in Shanghai, who selects and appoints from the list. The principals are directly appointed by the Japanese Emperor upon request from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, so the principals are appointed officials.

All training and teaching matters in the school are handled entirely by the principal. In addition to the principal, each school has one vice-principal to assist in handling training and teaching matters in the school. The vice-principal can act as the principal when the principal is on leave; when the principal retires, the vice-principal can be promoted to principal. In elementary schools, each school employs a government-certified nurse to oversee children's health and hygiene in the school.

A unique feature of the administration of each school is planned work. Each school formulates a work plan for the coming year in March; formulates a work plan for the coming month at the end of each month; and formulates a work plan for the coming week at the end of each week. The daily work is carried out in three stages: (1) Work before class each day: issue children's attendance records, pay attention to school announcements, monitors inspect the interior and exterior of the school building, protect the safety of naughty children, prepare teaching aids, attend staff meetings, and patrol the classroom. (2) Work after school each day: supervise and guide day students, report student absences, pay attention to school announcements, process children's grades, research guidance materials, schedule tomorrow's work, inspect the interior and exterior of the school building, extracurricular guidance and homework guidance, handle assigned affairs, research and self-cultivation. (3) Work during the day: conduct morning meetings, lead children's assembly and dispersal, check and record absent children, treat sick children, implement learning guidance, advise on training policies, apply learning tools, care for children, and guide children's lunch.

4. Revenue and Expenditure

The revenue and expenditure of Japanese schools in Shanghai are handled by the Residents' Association. The Residents' Association's revenue and expenditure items and documents are audited four times a year by the Audit Committee. The Audit Committee has seven expert members, who are elected by the Residents' Association's general annual meeting. The Audit Committee submits the audit results to the Japanese Consul-General in Shanghai for review. The final accounts for each fiscal year must also be submitted to the Residents' Association's general annual meeting and approved by the Consul-General.

The standard of tuition fees charged by each school is as follows:

Elementary School: Elementary and High Levels – Free
