Economic Supplement

The Depreciation of the French Franc and the Stability of Our Country's Foreign Exchange

— Jiang Jie

(I)

Recently, the French government's ban on the transportation of military supplies to Spain has triggered resentment from the Popular Front. Labor strikes have resurfaced, causing political turmoil, which has affected the status of the French franc and brought about another crisis. On September 7th, the selling pressure on the French franc suddenly intensified, causing a sharp decline in its exchange rate against the British pound. It fell from 76.43 francs per pound at the beginning of this month to 76.94 francs on the 17th. For the French franc, this is the lowest price this year. At the same time, capital is fleeing and panic is spreading. On the 9th and 11th of this month, a total of US$21,005,000 worth of gold flowed to the United States. Statistics for the flow to the United Kingdom have not yet been seen, but according to London telecommunications, the number of corporate deposits in French currency received by the Bank of England has been increasing daily.

The recent depreciation of the French franc, while seemingly caused by political and labor unrest, actually has a more fundamental cause. The fierce currency devaluation competition among countries in recent years, the unprecedented economic difficulties since France adhered to the gold standard, and the financial panic caused by the atmosphere of war, all fundamentally make it difficult to maintain the par value of the French franc. As long as it is affected by political volatility or speculative attacks, panic will immediately occur, and this has happened four times this year alone. Given the current political turbulence in Europe, it can be confidently predicted that French franc panics will continue to occur frequently in the future. Some argue that the depreciation of the French franc is temporary, and that once the political and labor unrest is resolved, the French franc will return to stability. However, this view overlooks the fundamental causes of the French franc crisis.

(II)

Due to the fluctuations of the French franc, a large amount of French francs were sold off in the European financial market and British pounds were purchased, which greatly increased the demand for British pounds and strengthened its exchange rate. The British-American exchange rate rose in tandem under these circumstances, rising from US$5.0325 per pound at the beginning of this month to US$5.065625 on the 17th. For the British pound, this is the highest price this year. In February of this year, the US dollar once fell, and the British-American exchange rate rose to US$5.02625, which is still far below the current exchange rate.

This situation clearly runs counter to the British policy of gradually depreciating the pound and is very unfavorable to the United Kingdom. Therefore, when the French franc panic started, the British Exchange Equalisation Account intervened to maintain the exchange rate, both to prevent the British-French exchange rate from rising excessively and to bring the British-American exchange rate back down. However, as of the 17th, the effectiveness of this British intervention has not been significant. The French franc price only experienced a slight rebound on the 10th, and then continued to fall. The US dollar followed the same pattern, as detailed in the table below:

British-French Exchange Rate British-American Exchange Rate

Francs per Pound Dollars per Pound

September 1st 76.43 5.0325

7th 76.56 5.04125

8th 76.75 5.055

9th 76.83 5.05875

10th 76.78 5.055

11th 76.84 5.05875

12th 76.84 5.05875

14th 76.84 5.06125

15th 76.91 5.065

16th 76.90 5.0625

17th 76.94 5.065625

From the table above, we can see the fluctuation of the spot price of the French franc. At this time, the forward price of the French franc is also very weak, which further reflects the bleak prospects of the French franc.

In the current triangular relationship between the British pound, US dollar, and French franc, it is very difficult for the United Kingdom to support the French franc and keep the price of the pound relatively low, because the foundation of the French franc is fundamentally fragile. The selling pressure on the French franc from various parties is not entirely due to speculation, but also due to a large volume of spot transactions in French francs. While the selling pressure was very intense during the panic, continued selling persisted even after the panic subsided, albeit at a slightly slower pace. Therefore, the trend of the French franc exchange rate is fundamentally downward, and the British Exchange Equalisation Account cannot improve it. Given this environment, the price of the British pound will only continue to rise, and the exchange rate between the British-French and British-American currencies will undoubtedly increase.

(III)

The continuous changes in the British-French exchange rate have a small impact on our country's currency relations, while the rise in the British-American exchange rate directly affects our country's foreign exchange rate. Originally, at the beginning of the currency reform, the Chinese currency was linked to the British pound, with one yuan of national currency fixed at one shilling and two and a half pence. The value of one yuan of national silver currency equivalent to US$0.2975 was obtained through the arbitrage of British-American exchange rates. The formula is as follows:

If the British-American exchange rate does not change, then our country's exchange rates against the British pound and the US dollar will be in a balanced state and can remain stable. However, the British-American exchange rate has recently fluctuated greatly. For example, in February of this year, the British-American exchange rate rose to US$5.02625. If China's foreign exchange rate had remained unchanged at this time, a contradiction would have arisen between the exchange rates against the British pound and the US dollar. Speculators could have made huge profits in Shanghai by using arbitrage methods. The method is as follows:

Profits obtained using arbitrage methods (Note 1)

Therefore, China had to choose between lowering the British exchange rate and raising the American exchange rate. At that time, China chose the latter method, raising the Chinese-American exchange rate from US$0.2975 per 100 Chinese yuan to US$0.3025, while maintaining the Chinese-British exchange rate at its original level.

Now that the British-American exchange rate has risen again, the exchange rates of one shilling and two and a half pence against the British pound and approximately 30 yuan against the US dollar, which have been in place since February of this year, have once again created a contradiction between the two, and the situation can be said to be no different from the last time. However, the method that our country should adopt is different.

This time, the legal exchange rate of the Central Bank has not changed, but the actual selling and buying prices have changed. On September 9th, Mr. Xi Demao, manager of the Sino-British Bank, issued a statement saying that the Central Bank, under the instructions of the Minister of Finance, would increase the difference between the legal price and the buying and selling prices of foreign exchange. Previously, the difference was one-eighth for the British pound, one-quarter for the US dollar, and one cent for the Japanese yen. Now, it has been changed to one-quarter for the British pound, one-half for the US dollar, and two cents for the Japanese yen, in order to prevent arbitrage speculation in the local market. At the same time, according to the author's investigation, the Central Bank's selling price for the British pound is one shilling, two pence, and one-quarter, and the buying price is one shilling, two pence, and three-quarters. The selling price for the US dollar is US$29.50, and the buying price is US$30.50.

The legal exchange rate is only an indication, and those who observe actual practice should take the bank's selling price as the standard. Judging by the selling price, the price of our country's currency is slightly lower than before. The Central Bank's daily selling prices are not published, so the daily selling prices of HSBC are listed here, and their trend is the same as the Central Bank's selling prices.

Daily Exchange Rates of HSBC

(Note) British Exchange Rate: Number of British Pounds Equal to 1 Yuan of Chinese Currency; American Exchange Rate: Number of Yuans of Chinese Currency Equal to 100 US Dollars; Japanese Exchange Rate: Number of Yuans of Chinese Currency Equal to 100 Japanese Yen; French Exchange Rate: Number of Yuans of Chinese Currency Equal to 100 French Francs

Observing the exchange rate changes in recent months, the stability of our country's foreign exchange is very significant, with the largest fluctuation not exceeding 1.1%. Although the change is very subtle, it is normal. Before September 9th, the pound exchange rate was still stable and unchanged. After the 9th, the pound exchange rate also changed. It can be seen that the new currency system is not a pound exchange standard system, and the Chinese-British exchange rate is not fixed.

Analyzing the content of this foreign exchange change, the stability of the exchange rate against the US dollar is noteworthy. According to the HSBC market, the exchange rates against the British pound, Japanese yen, and French franc have all moved, while the US dollar exchange rate has remained unchanged, which is the opposite of the situation in January of this year, when the British pound exchange rate was unchanged and the US dollar exchange rate was allowed to float. This point can be linked to the signing of the Sino-American Silver Agreement for consideration. Another point worth noting is that the exchange rate changes against the British pound and Japanese yen this time have both lowered the price of our country's currency. The author believes that this measure is beneficial to our country's trade, and that a gradual policy of low exchange rates should be adopted in the future. A gradual policy of low exchange rates is beneficial to trade and does not hinder financial stability.

Now it can be known that changes in international currencies will naturally affect our group's exchange situation. This is not only the case for our country, but for any country. Modern international finance is interwoven and interconnected, and no country can isolate itself from the influence of other major countries. So the influence is natural. The question is whether the changes in our country's exchange rate can be based on our country's interests. If so, then even if affected, we will still retain the autonomy of our currency, just like the United Kingdom. If not, then the harm will be infinite.

In today's era when countries use exchange rate policies as tools of economic warfare, our country must preserve this last line of defense.

—September 18th—

Note 1: This is purely calculated according to the legal exchange rate. In fact, there are still differences between the trade price and the cost price. However, this difference is usually very small, so when the exchange rate is out of balance by a corner, arbitrage can be profitable.

Note 2: July 1st and 2nd were holidays, so July 3rd was taken instead.

Review of the Bumper Harvest Problem

— Li Yinbei

(I) Introduction

Since the beginning of this spring, the spring famine problem in various places has been particularly serious due to the poor autumn harvest last year. Consequently, in the first quarter, the import of foreign rice reached 440,493 metric tons, used to relieve the food shortage. Recently, however, the situation has drastically changed. Since the sowing season this spring, the weather has been favorable, and no major disasters have occurred, leading to predictions of a nationwide bumper harvest this year. In late August, Minister of the Interior Jiang Zuobin reported on the bumper harvest issue during the 39th weekly memorial service for the late Premier Sun Yat-sen at the central government. He briefly stated: "Every year, we receive telegrams reporting disasters and famines from provinces across the country, pouring in incessantly. But this year is different. As of now, the Ministry of the Interior has not received a single document reporting a disaster or famine. Furthermore, the reports I have received privately indicate that all provinces across the country are experiencing a bumper harvest this year. I learned in Anhui that the province is expecting a 140% harvest this year. In Lu, I met with two central committee members from Jiangxi, Hubei, and Henan, who informed me that Jiangxi also expects a 140% harvest this year, and Hubei a full 100%. This situation is unprecedented in decades and is a cause for celebration for the people nationwide. However, with such a bountiful harvest, we should further improve our warehousing and management methods to prevent farmers from being harmed by low grain prices. Regarding the improvement of warehousing, the renovation of old warehouses, and the construction of new ones, the Ministry of the Interior has drafted regulations, which are currently being submitted to the Executive Yuan. Once approved, they will be disseminated to all provinces for implementation, ensuring that this unprecedented bumper harvest is not damaged by poor storage..." At the same time, during the weekly memorial service of the National Government, President of the Legislative Yuan Sun Ke also gave a similar report. (See Shen Bao, September 1) From this, we can observe that the hope of a nationwide bumper harvest this year is likely to materialize. Now, let's examine the issue of the bumper harvest below.

(II) General Review of the Bumper Harvest Problem

(1) The Bumper Harvest Problem and Economic Cycles

The method of agricultural management in our country remains in a state of tenancy farming. The abundance or scarcity of the harvest is left to "fate." Therefore, throughout history, years of abundance and scarcity have been like waves, with neither perpetual famine nor constant prosperity. As the saying goes, "After a year of famine comes a year of abundance," which is the idea. This situation closely resembles the cyclical nature of social and economic cycles. The following is a compilation of the agricultural situation and social and economic cycles in China since the Republic of China, tentatively compiled by Yao Qingsan:

It is noted that Yao's tentative compilation of the economic history of China is based on materials from China in the "Business Annals" co-edited by Professor Mitchell and Dr. Thorp of the United States. Therefore, the economic cycle is divided into four periods: (1) Prosperity, (2) Depression, (3) Recession (the transition from prosperity to depression), and (4) Revival (the transition from depression to prosperity). Since the Republic of China, there have been eleven years of bumper harvests. (Excluding leap years.) There has been a bumper harvest every three years on average. During the economic depression period, there were seven bumper harvests, accounting for 64% of the total number of bumper harvests since the Republic of China. During the economic recovery period, there were two bumper harvests, accounting for 18% of the total number of bumper harvests since the Republic of China. During the economic prosperity period, there were two bumper harvests, accounting for 18% of the total number of bumper harvests since the Republic of China. However, during the economic recession period, there has never been a bumper harvest. From this, we can infer that the abundance of harvests is a natural mechanism driven by the improvement of social and economic cycles, and it is also sufficient to tighten the original driving force of all economic organizations. Therefore, there are particularly many bumper harvests during the economic depression period, which is the principle that extremes beget their opposites.

The determination of a bumper harvest is the result of reduced disasters. By observing the previous table, it is clear that in years of floods and droughts, the harvest is inevitably poor. Conversely, the years are abundant. However, in 1928, there was a drought in the Northwest, but the rice harvest was still bountiful, which seems contradictory at first glance. It should be noted that the Northwest is not a major rice-producing area, and the drought in the first year was not enough to affect the overall situation. However, after two consecutive years of drought, the people in the rice-producing areas of the Huai River and Yangtze River basins transported grain to provide relief. As a result, it was impossible for Central and Southern China to remain prosperous alone. Therefore, in 1929 and 1930, the rice harvest nationwide was poor.

(2) The Bumper Harvest Problem and Seasonal Changes

Observing the supply and demand of rice throughout the year, the four months of September, October, November, and December are the season when the supply of rice exceeds demand, commonly known as the new grain market season. The four months of May, June, July, and August are the season when the demand for rice exceeds supply, commonly known as the lean season. Low grain prices harming farmers occur during the new grain market season, while high grain prices harming the people occur during the lean season. Therefore, the season most closely related to the bumper harvest problem is the new grain market season when the supply of rice exceeds demand. By examining the average price of new rice during the bumper harvest seasons since the Republic of China, we can often get a glimpse of the extent of farmers' losses.

Comparison of the Average Price of New Rice during Bumper Harvest Periods since the Republic of China with the Average Rice Price of the Current Year

Looking at the table above, the average rice price during the new grain market season is lower than the average rice price of the year in every year. However, during the new grain market season in 1919, the price of new rice was 6% higher than the average price of the year. This was because the European War had just ended, the Paris Peace Conference was signed, and countries purchased large quantities from rice-producing countries due to food shortages after the war. At the same time, our government abolished the ban on rice exports. As a result, large quantities of rice flowed out. Therefore, even during the new grain market season of a bumper harvest, there was still a phenomenon of demand exceeding supply. This is a special situation and cannot be taken as a standard.

(III) Review of This Year's Bumper Harvest Problem

(1) Forecast of This Year's Harvest

It is currently unknown how much rice will be produced this year. The estimates of 100% and 140% from various provinces are merely psychological speculations and cannot be regarded as reliable standards. However, based on the estimation of rice production in the last five years, this year's harvest may only slightly increase compared to the bumper harvest of 1933. Please see the table below for the rice production situation in the past five years:

It is noted that 1932 and 1933 were the most impressive years for rice harvests in the past five years. Therefore, the rice stored in the spring of 1934, according to experienced rice traders, amounted to as many as one million bags of foreign rice in Shanghai alone. Although not domestic rice, it was ultimately due to the bumper harvest of domestic rice that there was no sale. The rice stored in Wuxi was also about 1.3 million piculs, and it was said that Hunan had three years' worth of rice stored. (See Social and Economic Monthly, Volume 1, Issue 3) Furthermore, according to a report from the Jiangxi Economic Committee, at the end of 1933, Jiangxi produced 111,428,197 piculs of rice, so after deducting consumption within the province, there were still over a million piculs that could be transported out. The situation in other provinces was also similar. Regarding the yield per mu (unit of land area) in this year (1933), the rice planting area in 1933 was 279,905,000 mu, (see Agricultural Information Report of the Central Agricultural Experiment Station) and the average yield per mu was 3.5 shi (unit of volume) of grain.

As for the rice production situation this year, Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi spoke freely with a reporter from the New News Agency when he received him the other day, discussing the central government's financial situation. He said, "This year's agricultural harvest is due to heaven's help, but also half due to human effort. In recent years, the construction of water conservancy projects in various provinces, the expansion of planting areas, and the improvement of planting techniques have all increased production. Therefore, I hope that the people nationwide will not only be happy about this bountiful year but also pay close attention to how to increase production further. Because according to our statistics, there are no less than 400 million mu of arable land in our country, but only 150 million mu are currently used for cultivation!..." (See Shen Bao, September 7) Today, Kong's estimate of the current cultivated area and the 1,534,400,000 mu of the national crop area estimated by the former Directorate of Statistics of the Government are still the same. However, Kong did not mention whether the percentage of rice crop area in the national crop area has increased. According to the author's knowledge, the Statistical Bureau's survey period was four years ago. At that time, the bureau estimated the rice crop area to be 183,546,000 mu, accounting for 18% of the national crop area. Comparing it with the Agricultural Information Report of the Central Agricultural Experiment Station in 1933, the two seem to be consistent. However, since the central government vigorously implemented the policies of prohibiting drugs and opium after 1934, the land originally used for planting opium and other toxic substances has mostly been converted to planting food crops. But this political situation was after the Statistical Bureau's survey. Therefore, we speculate that the national rice crop area may have the potential to expand. Moreover, in some provinces, such as Guangdong, Guangxi, Jiangxi, and Fujian, the rice crop has two or even three harvests a year. If we follow the estimate of the Statistical Bureau, the actual rice crop area only accounts for 14% of the national crop area. Therefore, Lin Xichun estimated that it should be doubled to 28%. (See Social and Economic Monthly, Volume 2, Issue 3, pages 46) However, according to our speculation, the rice crop area should account for between 20% and 25% of the national crop area.

Now, let's assume that the rice crop area this year accounts for 24% of the national crop area. (The national crop area is still based on the estimate of the Statistical Bureau.) Then the rice planting area this year should be 368,256,000 mu. Assuming an average yield of 3.5 shi of grain per mu, the estimated harvest this year should be 1,288,896,000 piculs. This is an increase of 33% compared to the bumper harvest of 1932 and an increase of 31% compared to the bumper harvest of 1933. Whether this figure is reliable remains to be proven in the future. However, there is one issue that we cannot ignore: in provinces such as Guangdong, Fujian, Jiangxi, and Guangxi, there are two or even three harvests a year. If we consider the economic principle of the "Law of Diminishing Returns," the more harvests there are, the lower the yield will be. This is an immutable principle, and anyone with basic economic knowledge can understand it. Therefore, whether the yield per mu can consistently reach 3.5 shi of grain is a question. Furthermore, the yield of 3.5 shi was calculated based on the rice production and planting area in 1933. However, when the Central Agricultural Experiment Station surveyed the rice planting area, it is possible that people underreported or omitted their rice fields due to tax evasion. Furthermore, there is no consistent standard for calculating the area of fields in our country. Some use rice seedlings as the standard, measuring one mu by the number of seedlings that can be planted. Others use plow furrows as the standard, calculating the number of furrows in plowing as one mu. There are countless methods. With different calculation methods, the size of the fields varies. Therefore, there are reasons to doubt the yield of 3.5 shi of grain. This is another issue. According to experts' estimates, the productivity of our country's land is only higher than that of India. Before the improvement of production technology, the average yield per mu is only about 2 shi. This is another issue. Currently, our agricultural management methods remain under tenancy farming, which only reduces the productivity of the land and does not increase it. This year's bumper harvest is actually due to the favorable natural environment, not the result of human methods. Therefore, based on various observations, the estimated bumper harvest of rice this year is, at best, unlikely to exceed 100 million shi. If we estimate rice production at about 700 million shi based on the customary 73% conversion from grain to rice.

(2) Estimation of National Consumption

There is currently no official government estimate of the average annual consumption of rice by the people. Although there are unofficial estimates from private sources, they vary greatly and are inconsistent. Therefore, it is impossible to estimate the total annual consumption. Lin Xichun once synthesized materials from various sources and estimated that an average of 2.2 piculs of rice per person per year would be sufficient. He also calculated that the national population is 450 million, and the rice-eating population accounts for one-third, or 300 million. Therefore, the annual demand for rice is 660,000,000 piculs.

According to Lin's estimated figures, this year's bumper harvest of rice, in addition to national consumption, would have a surplus of 40 million piculs. However, in reality, this is not the case. According to the Central Agricultural Experiment Station, in our country, rice, in addition to being used for legitimate human consumption, is also used for brewing alcohol. The amount accounts for 18% of the total amount used for human food. Based on this calculation, of the 700 million piculs of rice harvested this year, 126 million piculs must be deducted by private wineries for brewing alcohol. Only 574 million piculs are available for legitimate human consumption! There is still a shortage of 86 million piculs of rice, which cannot be obtained. Otherwise, there will be a famine for more than three months, or more than 30 million people will have to rely on foreign rice.

(3) A Glimpse of Surpluses and Deficits in Various Regions

From a geographical perspective, the richest rice-producing areas in our country are the provinces south of 32 degrees north latitude, such as Sichuan, Hunan, Jiangxi, and Anhui, which are all rice-surplus provinces. By examining the domestic trade of rice in these provinces during the bumper harvest year of 1933, we can get a glimpse of their rice surpluses.

1933 was a year of bumper rice harvest. Anhui Province exported 3,491,339 piculs of rice to other provinces, making it the province with the largest surplus of food in the country that year. Hunan Province has always been a rice-producing area. There is an old saying, "If Hunan and Guangdong are prosperous, the world will be fed!" That year, the province exported 618,101 piculs to other provinces, ranking second among the food-surplus provinces, while only 46 piculs were imported into Hunan from other provinces! Jiangxi Province exported 530,941 piculs to other provinces that year, ranking third, while 3,793 piculs were imported into Jiangxi from other provinces. Sichuan exported 9,756 piculs to other provinces. The total amount exported to other provinces by the above four provinces was 4,650,377 piculs, while the total amount imported into these provinces from other provinces was 3,839 piculs, less than one-thousandth of the exported amount. In 1933, the national rice production was 984,190,000 piculs, and the surplus of rice in these four provinces accounted for 5% of the national rice production. However, some of the rice exported from these four provinces that year had already been processed into brown rice, so the actual surplus was more than 5% of the national production. According to our speculation, it should be around 7-8%. As for this year's situation, can the rice surplus in these four provinces be higher than in 1933? According to our research and estimation from various aspects, at most, it will only be equal to 1933. This is because 1933 inherited the bumper harvest of 1932. Due to various reasons, the surplus rice from the bumper harvest of 1932 could not be transported to other provinces. Therefore, in 1933, in addition to the bumper harvest of that year, the surplus grain from the bumper harvest of 1932 could be transported out of the province in a relaxed manner. If we compare the amount of rice exported to other provinces by these four provinces in 1932 with that in 1933, it will be clearer.

The national rice production in 1932 was 969,080,000 piculs, accounting for 98.5% of the national rice production in 1933. The harvest was also considerable. However, since the new grain market season was already in the last quarter of 1932, it was impossible to transport all of it to other provinces due to time constraints. Moreover, at this time, the rice in various provinces was in a season of supply exceeding demand, so there was no market for importing rice from other provinces. Therefore, although the stored grain was abundant, it could only be left for the following year (i.e., 1933) to be exported out of the province. Therefore, the amount of rice exported from the province in 1933 actually accounted for the total amount of one and a half years. From this point of view, is this year's bumper harvest a result of inheriting the surplus from last year's bumper harvest? If last year's harvest was not as bountiful as that of 1932, then the surplus of rice in these four provinces this year may not be as good as that of 1933.

Furthermore, in terms of self-sufficient provinces, Jiangsu, Hebei, Hubei, and Guangxi had mixed domestic trade inflows and outflows amid the bumper harvest in 1933. Although Jiangsu is a rice-producing area, its population density is higher than that of other provinces in recent years. According to experts' estimates, it can only be self-sufficient. Even in a bumper harvest, the export is not much. Hebei, Hubei, and Guangxi are not very important rice-producing provinces, but there may be no problem in self-sufficiency. As for Guangdong, Fujian, Zhejiang, Shandong, and Yunnan, they are all rice-deficient provinces. Moreover, the Southwest is a low-tax area for foreign rice, so a large amount of foreign rice is imported every year. The above provinces' situations are all obtained after the analysis of the bumper harvest in 1933. As for their situation this year, it is difficult to say for sure at one time. However, in general, rice can definitely be surplus in surplus provinces, but rice can hardly be self-sufficient and have a surplus in deficit provinces. This can be asserted.

(IV) Conclusion

In summary, when it comes to so-called bumper harvests in our country throughout history, people often mistakenly believe that there is an opportunity for rice self-sufficiency. Actually, this is a big mistake. For China to truly achieve self-sufficiency in rice, it must first adjust production technology and expand the cultivated area. The reason for low grain prices harming farmers is entirely due to the temporary phenomenon of supply exceeding demand during the new grain market season. From an economic point of view, this is not unreasonable. Tang Wenkai believed that low grain prices can harm farmers and benefit farmers. The crux of the matter is whether farmers have a surplus to exchange for usable goods after paying all production costs during low grain prices. If there is a sufficient surplus to compensate for all the necessary material equipment, then low grain prices are not harmful. Therefore, he advocated increasing agricultural output and reducing burdens. However, due to the large scale of the matter, it was difficult to find support. In order to solve this year's bumper harvest problem, we will temporarily start with a symptomatic treatment and balance the supply and demand of new grain. In other words, we will start promoting "simple farmers' associations" in rice-surplus provinces, and control transportation and sales in rice self-sufficient and rice-deficit provinces.

The method of storing grain to relieve famine has been practiced in China for a long time. However, due to the corruption and embezzlement by local bullies after the decline of warehouse administration in the late Qing Dynasty, the private warehousing industry gradually declined. In 1928, the Executive Yuan drafted warehousing measures, stipulating that the national warehouse grades should be (1) National Reserve Warehouse; (2) Provincial Reserve Warehouse; (3) County Warehouse; (4) District Warehouse; (5) Township Warehouse, and other five categories. However, due to various reasons, it was not fully realized. The author believes that the warehousing industry should be vigorously promoted. However, in the abnormal environment of this time and place, we must also consider it. Therefore, it is advocated that the establishment of national warehouses, provincial warehouses, and county warehouses be continued for those that have already been established, and those that have not yet been established should be postponed. This type of warehouse mostly adopts a large-scale centralized storage system for grain, and the safety issue is worth considering. In the event of an emergency, this huge amount of stored grain will inevitably be bombed! Therefore, the highest principles for running the warehousing business at present should be "simplicity," "universality," and "distributed storage." Moreover, in terms of the current actual people's strength, these three are also easier to implement. As for the method of popularizing this simple agricultural warehouse, in addition to using old warehousing funds and local public funds, we should also use the surrounding economic environment, such as cooperatives, railways, highways, and postal savings bureaus. Because these entities have production relations with rice, or transportation and sales relations, or financial lending relations, they can all use their spare capacity to assist farmers in popularizing the establishment of agricultural warehouses.

Regarding the location of simple agricultural warehouses, in this year's bumper harvest problem, rice-surplus provinces should be the center, such as Hunan, Jiangxi, and Anhui provinces, which should be given serious attention. Because if farmers in these surplus provinces can keep their own grain and not dump it to other provinces unsystematically, the grain prices in self-sufficient provinces can be greatly reduced during the new grain market season, and grain prices will not fall drastically. In grain-deficient provinces, the provincial government authorities should manage the unified transportation and sales, and consider the shortage in the province as the standard for adding foreign rice. In short, the central work in rice-surplus provinces is to popularize simple agricultural warehouses. In rice-deficient provinces, the central work is to control transportation and sales. In self-sufficient provinces, the government manages the buying and selling of rice. The whole country is united and cooperates. Then this year's bumper harvest problem can be safely transitioned.

Spring and Autumn

Anecdotes: Autumn Feelings

— Zhou Guochang

The rustling autumn wind blows the leaves on the trees, one by one, causing the velvety grass to tremble and change color. A flock of wild geese soar in the sky, making a clear and mournful sound, which is transmitted into my eardrums, instantly adding to my infinite sorrow.

Summer goes and autumn arrives, which is originally a natural phenomenon in a year, but time passes so quickly that time has passed and circumstances have changed in an instant. See how creatures grow vigorously in spring and summer, but gradually wither and turn yellow in autumn. Just like a person's life, when he is young and promising, he does not engage in serious business, and wastes his precious time in vain; once his hair turns white and many wrinkles appear on his face, although he wants to make progress, his spirit declines, and he finally achieves nothing. Thinking of the past, he regrets it too late and can only sigh.

I hope that we young people, when we are young and strong, work hard for your future and do not waste precious time, lest we feel the sorrow of being old and sad.

Random Musings on Autumn

— Hua Ling

Of the four seasons, I believe it is not spring that is most worth cherishing, but autumn. The reason is that spring is tiresome. The vexations of life often creep into the human world along with the tiresome spring. Only when the autumn wind rises are these vexations swept away along with the falling leaves. Thus, what we feel in autumn is a sense of ease and inexplicable comfort.

Human vision needs adjustment. Therefore, in winter, we have the boundless white snow covering the universe, giving us the pleasure of a change of environment. In spring and summer, what we see are nothing but green branches and leaves, purple pistils and red flowers. After being surrounded by red flowers and green leaves for two long seasons, we enter a scene of yellow leaves and bare branches in autumn. Although sensitive poets cannot help but feel sentimental about their own lives, I believe this is precisely the adjustment of vision that nature gives us, and it can also be said to be an intimation that we must seek adjustment in life.

Superficially speaking, autumn can also be said to be an unpretentious season. It does not require the coolness needed in summer, nor the artificial warmth needed in winter. In autumn, the flow of blood in the human body is not as rapid as in spring. The function of growth gradually enters a state of stillness, but it is not as dry and lacking in vitality as in winter. Therefore, autumn is a model of frugality without stinginess.

If our praise for spring is for a plump beauty, then for autumn, we should say it is for a lean old man. The mountains have faded in color, but are not yet bare. The trees have lost their shady green leaves, but have not yet revealed their dry branches. On the earth, although there is no longer the chirping of orioles, the chirping of crickets and the long cries of solitary geese, one or two at a time, decorate the scene without the desolation of winter. Therefore, autumn is a lean old man, whose spirit is still so vigorous, not at all like winter, which shows such decrepitude.

But when the autumn wind rises, wealthy families are busy preparing to eat crabs and admire chrysanthemums, while the poor, with only a worn-out padded jacket and trousers, and only an old cotton quilt, are still keeping them in pawnshops, unable to redeem them, and are worrying about it. In large shops, banners of autumn sales flutter in the wind, and under the neon lights in the large windows, the smiling faces of expensive goods seem to shine constantly, while the poor can only bite their lower lips, staring blankly at these things, watching the gentlemen and ladies drive away fully loaded. – Perhaps this still indicates that autumn is quite snobbish?

Autumn Clouds

— Fang Zheng

Autumn clouds are full of flavor. Since I was a child, I have had an inextricable bond with my home. Later, when I entered society, I was fortunate enough to work in the countryside where I could see the sun. Therefore, "autumn clouds" gave me a deep understanding. Whenever there was a quiet morning glow, or a dusk "sending off the setting sun in the sound of oars," I would always walk alone to the suburbs to appreciate it for a while. If it rained, although I stopped my usual lessons, I couldn't help but feel as unhappy as if I had lost a beloved thing!

Because autumn clouds are so lovely, they change at any time and in countless ways on the vast sky. It would be most appropriate to describe them as magicians.

The best places to see autumn clouds in my hometown are Mount Qiyun and Mount Huang. It is said that because the mountains are high, when you reach the top, the clouds are already in front of your eyes. Not to mention seeing them, it is easy to catch them with your hands. But unfortunately, I have never tried it, and I dare not fully introduce what it tastes like.

People often use autumn clouds to compare human relationships, but today's human relationships are simply not as good as autumn clouds! Reading Xu Jialin's letter to Lu Jianzhi in "Qiu Shui Xuan Chi Du," he said: "As a brother, I call on Jiang Bo every day to ask for help; I never thought that human affairs are like autumn clouds, and human feelings are like flowing water. In ordinary times, we value friendship and keep our promises; but when it comes to money, they turn their backs on me as if they don't know me. Since I asked for help, I have knocked on their doors almost ten times, but nine times they have not opened." Although it is not entirely using "autumn clouds" as a metaphor, the human relationships of that time have been fully expressed. If Xu Gong were still alive today, I really don't know what kind of clouds he would use to curse the state of the world?

Although I like to appreciate autumn clouds, I can't help but take a cold breath after reading Xu Gong's letter.

An Unlonely Autumn

— Zhou Xian

"The weather is cool but not cold" is a phrase unique to autumn. Because in autumn, there is no terrible heat like in summer, nor terrible cold like in winter, so autumn can be said to be the most lovely season of the year. Moreover, there is a common saying, "Spring blooms, autumn fruits." Indeed, the cotton for clothing and the millet for food are all harvested in this autumn, rewarding the farmers for their hard work throughout the year, and enriching the necessities of life for those with round heads and square feet to keep out the cold. Therefore, autumn can also be said to be our golden season.

In autumn, our lives can be said to be quite unlonely. "The weather is cool but not cold" is a good season for travel. Whether it is on the mountain or by the water, there is a unique and refreshing scene in the clear autumn light. The raging waves and the faint white clouds are all good material for the traveler's camera. The scarlet maple leaves are even better subjects for the traveler to compose poems. Therefore, the activity of travel groups in various places during this season is naturally expected. And the large number of travelers traveling to various places may be of some help to the rural economy that is on the verge of bankruptcy.

In the autumn garden, one will not feel lonely because of the withering of all kinds of flowers. You only need to plant a few autumn chrysanthemums, which have always had the style of noble scholars, in the courtyard or by the fence. Then you can be sure that in the atmosphere of cold dew and frost, you will not have to worry about the lack of colorful flowers to please the eye. In terms of eating, the "unintestined gentleman," the crab, becomes fat and plump day by day, crawling across the fishermen's huts in the autumn wind, and is placed on plates for us to enjoy. In terms of playing, the cricket, which has the title of "general," constantly emits tempting chirping sounds in front of the steps and under the walls, waiting for people to catch and play with.

At the same time, in this autumn season, we have the Mid-Autumn Festival with its full moon, and the Double Ninth Festival for ascending to high places to avoid vulgarity. After being busy with this, we are busy with that. The short autumn light will surely slip away easily. Even to say something unambitious, even if one is suffering from poverty and illness, living a life away from home, lying in bed with a quilt, with only the stove and a lamp as companions, there are still the roaring autumn wind and the autumn rain knocking on the window, very diligently accompanying you to relieve your loneliness away from home.

It is really too lovely – our unlonely autumn.

—

Huan Chao Luan Feng (Phoenixes Re-nesting)

The Wonton Seller

— Nong

"Doo-doo-doo."

The wonton seller is like a clock. When people have worked all day and are about to rest, he comes along smiling and says, "You've worked hard all day, come and eat wontons." If you don't have any money with you, he will say to you, "Old customer, I'll give you a bowl on credit." He does business so politely, which earns him a lot of goodwill from the customers.

He is only a young man in his twenties this year. A few years ago, he escaped from Shenyang to Shanghai with his father, who was in his fifties, under the hail of bullets. He doesn't gamble, drink, or visit prostitutes, but he has a special hobby – reading. He often puts books like "Water Margin" and "Dream of the Red Chamber" on his wonton stand. He tells me that he borrowed them by going to the library entrance. He said, "Besides supporting my old father, I use the rest of the money I earn to buy books."

He studied at a middle school in Shenyang for a year and a half. People asked him why he didn't become a primary school teacher to make a comfortable living. He replied, "Doesn't 'Education of Love' say that a shoemaker who can make good shoes is better than an incompetent university professor or an incompetent lawyer?"

One Saturday afternoon, he was walking hurriedly with two prescriptions in his hand, his face covered with sorrow. That amiable smile that he usually had was nowhere to be seen. People said that his father had suddenly contracted the plague and his condition was very serious. As a result, the son was as anxious as an ant on a hot pot.

Two weeks have passed, and I haven't seen the wonton seller's shadow. My heart seems to feel a strange loneliness. Here, I sincerely wish them peace and well-being!

Water Red Water Caltrop

— (Lake Beggar)

When the autumn wind rises, the water caltrop turns purple. They are recommended to the market during the season, accounting for a large proportion of the rural aquatic income. There are many low-lying ponds in Jiangnan. Besides farming, people regard this as a source of profit. Therefore, clear streams around the houses and ponds all over the fields are full of green leaves, supplementing the autumn harvest. The water caltrop produced in Xiang Lake is known together with water shield and lotus root, which goes without saying. Even in the various counties of Kuaiji, the floating ports and rivers are of unknown numbers of thousands of acres. By the end of summer, green surrounds all sides, making people feel that the water country scenery has a special charm. When the繁花白了 (unsure of meaning), a red corner emerges. Harvesting boats float out like ducklings, with long poles and short skirts, mostly women in charge. They sing impromptu songs without accompaniment, which are more interesting than the mountain tea songs in the wilderness. In autumn, there are many red reeds on the beach. When someone asks if there are those who insert them into their black hair to compete with the beauty of the reeds, the women laugh and scold together. When the pole tilts and the boat lists, water splashes on their skirts, they are in great commotion. At this time, the autumn sun is still harsh, roasting their skin pitifully, but they float east and west, not returning until the boat is full. When the evening glow is brilliant and their slender hands are tired, some even have bloody fingers, congealing into the remaining glow, but they do not think it is hard. River lanterns are brightly lit, and the water caltrop market becomes noisy. People carrying burdens on their shoulders jostle against each other. Tomorrow, you will hear vendors everywhere on the streets and alleys calling out "Water Red Water Caltrop." It is said that one acre of water caltrop pond can yield one or two tens of gold. Those who work in this industry need not worry about wind and rain, nor about insect damage. In spring and winter rainy seasons, they can also collect fish, shrimp, reeds, and other benefits. In the past, Zhou He had the line "an old business, a pond of water caltrop." Truly, on the mountain peaks and by the water's edge, if one can exert their strength, they will have no shortage of food and clothing.

When I first arrived in Qiantang, I saw that most of the water caltrop on the market was said to be produced in West Lake. The sellers also often falsely claimed this to deceive customers. In fact, West Lake has no water caltrop, it is transferred from Xiang Lake and Hushu area. Every Mid-Autumn Festival, when the moon is bright and the fragrance of clothing floats on the shore, the water caltrop and lotus root business is at its peak. People sit in the open air by the rippling mirror-like water, peeling and eating, and tourists all seem to replace mooncakes with them. Therefore, the usual dozens of texts per pound must be doubled on that evening. Near Hangzhou, water caltrop are mostly green, but east of Zhejiang, they are all胭脂艷 (unsure of meaning). This is probably due to the difference in water quality? If we talk about the sweet and crisp taste, the round water caltrop of South Lake are the best. They break easily when touched with the teeth, surpassing the taste of lotus root, and are unparalleled. Sometimes, the cool waves reflect the candle, and the beautiful ladies linger. They pick and offer the water caltrop to the guests, making people feel that the leisurely flavor is even better than serving silver cakes with wine. Lake caltrop have been recorded since the Tang Dynasty. Changgu's poem says: "One acre of white caltrop flowers in South Lake." I used to have a foolish idea: if I could return to my hometown one day, I would definitely open a ten-acre pond, specializing in planting water caltrop, lotus root, fish, shrimp, etc., and plant mulberry trees around the shore. Then I could sing and drink freely, which would be no different from the people above Xi Huang (a legendary ruler). Since I have lived in the world and experienced much, I know that this wish is not allowed. Even if I could get it, would the followers of Tao Yuanming allow me to survive in this world?

Autumn Night on the Huangpu River

— Ya Fei

One new autumn evening, a group of three of us boarded the small train parked at Tiantong'an Bridge, letting it carry us away from a corner of this great metropolis.

The train was like a centipede, meandering along the two rails, gradually climbing into the vast wilderness. Some rivers and villages quickly flew past the train window. The gentle autumn wind, like the breath of a young girl, drilled in through the window, lightly kissing our faces.

We got off the train at Paotaiwan Station, stepping on this last sunset, facing the evening wind blowing from the sea, and quietly walked towards the sea. A light feeling floated lightly into our consciousness.

Poets love the sea because of its greatness and majesty, which can inspire life. The roaring of the sea and the surging of the waves can open up the secrets of the universe and break the dumb riddles of nature.

We strolled along the seashore. The meadows and famous embankments were crowded with idle urban men and women. This great sea unfolded before us. The faint shadows of sails in the misty depths and the white gulls flying across the sea and sky seemed like a mysterious dream. The tower lamp on the embankment lit up, as if it was a guiding light for our future, giving us a little light in the darkness. As night deepened, people gradually began to flow along the seashore. The surging tide and the howling sea breeze played together to form the symphony of the sea.

"Listening to the tide on a moonlit night, the clothes are thin and unable to withstand the cold." So, we boarded the last evening boat back to Shanghai to enjoy the cool. The steamer left the pier in the midst of the clamor of voices, breaking through the waves and heading towards the river. It went from the Wusong River to Yangshupu. On the river, only small steamers could be seen, shuttling back and forth. The scattered lights were like sparse fishing lights, tilting and swaying with the waves. The sharp whistle roared so loudly that it almost shattered our eardrums.

After the steamer sailed into the Yangshupu area, the river became very lively. Several foreign cruisers stood in the middle of the river, and countless sailors were huddled on the decks, singing tragic battle songs or decadent love songs. The small steamers in the middle of the river were whistling, which inevitably aroused a feeling of desolation. Several rowboats were racing in the undulating waves as if they were going against the current, as if they were in danger of being overturned by the waves at any time! The towering skyscrapers on both sides of the Puxi and Pudong rivers were closely arranged, and the dazzling lights were blinking like the stars in the sky. The red and green neon lights trembled like a dream in front of our eyes. The voices of people and cars were clearly transmitted from the shore. So, we had returned to the embrace of the great metropolis.

Era of Medicine

Couple's Knowledge

— By Yao Erchang, MD, University of Pennsylvania, USA

The Eve of a Couple's First Sexual Encounter

How should the husband prepare to make his wife happy? Everyone should also take responsibility and be prepared to be a mother.

Even though we have already discussed many important topics about couple's knowledge, for the sake of making this issue extremely clear, it is necessary to discuss it further. Indeed, there are countless matters that need to be resolved between the two sexes. If we can carefully prepare for the most suitable and scientific methods before marriage, undoubtedly all post-marital disputes can be overcome one by one, resulting in a happy marriage life. Otherwise, the life after marriage will lose happiness, and who knows, one day it will turn into strangers again. Therefore, to avoid this tragedy from happening, we must first enrich ourselves with some knowledge necessary for health. Husbands cannot ignore the hygiene of the maturation period, especially the hygiene of the development of reproductive organs. Generally, the penis, testicles, prostate, seminal vesicles, etc. can develop properly. The reason is that the gonads secrete an endocrine fluid that promotes the development of reproductive organs. Therefore, the bad habit of masturbation during maturation often causes nocturnal emission and loss of seed secretion fluid. The reproductive organs will decline and stop developing. In addition, or due to congenital deficiencies, or as a result of excessive indulgence, not only will there be no satisfactory sexual organ development, but also after entering formal sexual life, premature ejaculation and impotence will cause you to fall into bursts of pain, and the other party will also be harmed, depriving her of the elasticity and stimulation of sexual life, and even unable to enjoy it!

However, the responsibilities of men towards women are also extremely important. Germany and Italy Encourage Childbirth

— Me

There was once a Confucian scholar who had no sons. He asked Ji Xiaolan for advice. Xiaolan replied, "This matter is entirely human desire and has no natural principles. You always hold the words 'natural principles' in your heart, so you cannot have a son. Look at animals, they move according to the season, and they are always successful because of this. From this, we can see that the way of childbirth is purely natural, and there is nothing to force or encourage."

At the annual convention of the German Socialist Party held on the 12th, leader Hitler gave a speech to 20,000 female party members, saying that any woman who can produce seven healthy and lively children has made a greater contribution to our nation than the most famous female lawyer. Hitler's words have great truth because one more healthy and lively citizen means one more strength for the country. If these 20,000 women each have seven children, they will get 140,000 strong citizens, which will add a different kind of splendor under the swastika flag.

Also, on the 12th, Italy held a meeting chaired by Prime Minister Mussolini and passed a new law to increase the birth rate in Italy. Afterwards, government and municipal positions will be given to married people first, and provincial and municipal governments will allocate funds to subsidize marriage and childbirth. Students and mothers of triplets will be given awards by the government. Fathers with eight children will have their children's education fees waived. This newly promulgated law is nothing more than an attempt to encourage childbirth, not only encouraging childbirth but also finding ways to support their lives after childbirth. Is this not a perfect way to encourage childbirth?

Therefore, I thought of the teachings of Mencius in our country, which are the same as those of Hitler and Mussolini. Mencius said, "There are three unfilial acts, and having no descendants is the greatest." Why is having no descendants the greatest of the three unfilial acts? Although Mencius did not explicitly say it, it is simply because if the bloodline is cut off, the ancestors will have no descendants to offer sacrifices. Later generations of sex fanatics interpret this meaning as: first, to create life for the world, second, to extend the bloodline of the ancestors, and third, to maintain ethical norms for the family. However, this kind of argument was still the saying of the patriarchal society at that time. If it is interpreted with the current national socialist consciousness, it must be: first, to create welfare for the people, second, to increase the strength of the country, and third, to store up sharp weapons for killing. The times are different, so the applications are also different.

Why do Hitler and Mussolini want to encourage childbirth? Nothing more than to wage war, to sacrifice, to give their lives on the battlefield, to achieve their ambitious goals and hopes. However, the present is a world of scientific warfare. If war breaks out, the defeated country will inevitably sacrifice countless lives, and even the victorious country will suffer incalculable losses. Therefore, the encouragement of childbirth by Hitler and Mussolini is actually encouraging sacrifice. Are the women of Germany and Italy striving to give birth to meet the expectations of Hitler and Mussolini?

Questioning the Simple and Convenient Public Dining Hall for People's Livelihood in This City

— Xishan

(Special Report from this Newspaper) In the city, many laborers who work like animals, their meager daily wages, in this expensive Shanghai, probably cannot even afford an ordinary meal.

Page 20

At the same time, due to the decline of the countryside and the depression of all industries in recent years, the number of hungry and unemployed people in the city is increasing day by day. In this situation, a public dining hall where one can get a sufficient meal for a low price is indeed urgently needed.

The Simple and Convenient Public Dining Hall for People's Livelihood in this city was created for the hungry masses of society in this situation. The organizer of the hall is Mr. Ling Youxian, an ordinary businessman, but he is very enthusiastic about social causes. Yesterday, I paid a special visit to his residence to inquire about the organization and overview of the Public Dining Hall. He explained the reasons for the establishment of the hall and everything inside very thoroughly.

The establishment of the Public Dining Hall has two reasons: (1) Due to the recent decline in the market and the increasing difficulty in people's livelihoods, the establishment of the Public Dining Hall hopes to directly reduce the consumption of common people. (2) In order to reduce the suffering of unemployed youth, the service personnel of the dining hall recruit ambitious young people and provide them with training and education to ensure that they have the ability to improve themselves.

The Public Dining Hall has been open for more than a year, and the number of diners has gradually increased, from fifty or sixty people per day to more than two hundred. Most of the diners are rickshaw pullers, laborers, and unemployed people. The dining hall sells two meals a day, lunch from 11:00 AM to 2:00 PM, and dinner from 6:00 PM to 10:00 PM. The dining hall currently has two locations, both of which borrow space from vegetable markets. Tangjiawan Vegetable Market in West Gate is the first dining hall, and Lishe Vegetable Market on Lujiabang Road is the second dining hall. These two vegetable markets are under the jurisdiction of charitable organizations, so they are very convenient to rent. After the daily vegetable market is completed in the two vegetable markets, they are converted into dining halls.

The service personnel of the dining hall, in addition to the kitchen staff, total more than ten people in the two locations, all of whom are unemployed young people who have received considerable education. They mostly feel the difficulties of life after unemployment, so they are very willing to serve and do not feel ashamed of their low status. In terms of treatment, in addition to providing them with food, clothing, and accommodation, they are also given education in the morning.

According to Mr. Ling, the funding for the dining hall is entirely his own responsibility. According to recent statistics, the first dining hall has about one hundred and dozens of diners per day, and the second dining hall has more than ninety, totaling more than two hundred in both locations. All the rice and dishes in the hall are sold at cost. The prices set for each meal are: white rice is sold for 10 copper coins per large can, 7 coins per medium can, vegetable dishes are 3 coins per plate, meat dishes are 8 coins per plate, soup is 3 coins per bowl, and fermented bean curd is 10 coins per piece. Most diners can have enough with a medium can of white rice and a plate of vegetables, so the cost per meal does not exceed four cents.

At the same time, I wanted to know about the equipment of the dining hall, so I wanted to go to the Tangliangwan Vegetable Market to see the first dining hall. It is a very simple dining hall that is built around the perimeter of the vegetable market. The entrance is the ticket purchase place, and diners must first purchase tickets there and then exchange the tickets for meals. The internal equipment is also quite complete. The cans and dishes for serving rice and dishes are all white porcelain. The storage of vegetables is also in line with the conditions of cleanliness. In the dining hall, there are several wooden long tables that can accommodate 150 people dining at the same time. The vegetables sold daily are also often changed. Vegetable dishes are mostly bean sprouts, vegetables, taro, tofu, and edamame. Meat dishes include yellow croaker, salted fish, and soy-braised shredded pork. All kinds of vegetables and meat are completely purchased fresh, and great attention is also paid to seasoning to make them suitable for the hygiene and taste of the public.

In the southern suburbs of the dining hall, there is also a parking lot because most of the diners for dinner at the first dining hall are rickshaw pullers. To avoid the loss of vehicles, the dining hall specifically hires a person to take care of them. When the rickshaw pullers leave their vehicles, they take a tag, and when they pick up the vehicle, they exchange the tag for the vehicle. This can also allow the rickshaw pullers to eat with peace of mind.

Finally, I felt that the establishment of the Simple and Convenient Public Dining Hall for People's Livelihood has indeed given great benefits to the urban poor. However, there seems to be a lack of such dining halls in Shanghai. Currently, there are only two locations in the South City. If they can be established everywhere in Huxi, Zhabei, and throughout the city, that would be the great happiness of the urban common people.

Pig

— Yunhai

This year is a year of abundance.

The rice fields are growing fat and big, and the ears of rice are full like pearl rice, and the deep orange-yellow color makes the eyes of the farmers shine. During the harvest, people are singing mountain songs and working happily.

Now, it hasn't been long since the harvest was completed. The grains have been threshed, some are spread on the threshing floor to bask in the sun, and some have been loaded into baskets, ready to be transported out and pay the grain.

However, it was at this time that the rice market gave them a bolt from the blue. When there is no rain people complain to heaven, when there is big water people hate the Dragon King for playing tricks, but, it is a year of abundance, and the price of grain has fallen from four yuan to three yuan and six, making the farmers angry. — This year, it's really impossible to get justice.

The good times of the harvest disappeared somehow, and the swarthy faces of the people turned a darker shade of blue. Chenjia Village, like the eve of a storm, was covered tightly by low, dark clouds. The people under it could not breathe, and even dared not sigh loudly.

Time is getting tighter and tighter, and the news that the officials who were urging the grain and collecting land rent were coming to the countryside, like the magic of the snake tail dragon, stirred up the entire Chenjia Village.

Uncle Gui couldn't think of a better way, so he had to bite the bullet and discuss it with his wife.

"Agou, the grain collectors will probably come to the countryside in the next few days. Today I just happened to go to the market, and I was thinking of selling the pig you raised and settling the account."

"Are you crazy?" This woman could not bear to part with the pig he had raised with so much effort, so she replied like this. "He is my life, I won't sell him!"

"If you don't sell him, we can't pay the taxes!"

"Tell them to take the grain. It's not enough even if they take a few more dan. Does that mean those who farm have to lose their lives? I won't sell him!"

"Agou, there's no way out of this! Don't talk about the pig, if it's after a disaster year, even if Agou is sold, it won't be enough to pay that life-threatening rent!"

The man was sighing, but the woman started wailing.

"Heaven is forcing me to my death."

Uncle Gui gritted his teeth, carried the piglet, and came to the market in a fit of anger.

He passed by the tailor shop, the Daji Grocery Store, and Chen Laotong was telling the news there. —

"Chen Daniu's boss, those short guys, hey, I heard that they recently robbed some of our places again. I can't remember so much. The newspapers in the provincial capital are selling very well! Damn it, now they don't have to pay taxes to transport goods, look —"

He pointed his mouth towards the foreign goods store that had just opened across the street.

"Eighteen generations of ancestors brought these goods from there. They sell them so cheap, I don't even have enough for my capital. The people in the provincial capital call this smuggling, smuggling your mother's rotten stinking X!"

This news is indeed very new. In a while, it spread all over the market, and the people were a little angry.

"There's no way out, it's death either way, I can't care about so much."

These were the words of Daniu and the others, and Chen Laotong nodded slightly when he passed by.

Uncle Gui didn't quite understand what Laotong and the others were talking about, he just thought that they were just some "news." But later, when he inquired about the price at the rice shop, he heard the shopkeepers saying.

"This year is really a plague year! A good year is deceiving people, even we wouldn't have thought that the price of grain would fall so badly."

"I heard that someone is manipulating it in the dark."

"That Chinese and foreign grocery store sent people out to buy a lot!"

"Someone is playing tricks, no wonder the market has become so chaotic in an instant!"

The old man sighed, but the young man widened his eyes, bit his teeth angrily, and shook his fist in the air a few times.

The old farmer Uncle Gui also felt confused. A heat rushed to his throat, a little itchy.

When he came to the pig pen, when the old shopkeeper told him the price, he was so angry that he couldn't help but the fire rushed straight up.

"Isn't this less than half?" — He said angrily and stubbornly.

"Yes, Uncle Gui!" The person who bought the pig knew his difficulties. "It's not that I'm reducing your price. There's really no way out, there's no market in the provincial capital either, we can't do anything!"

His heart was firm, and he wanted to take the pig back. But, when he changed his mind, the life-threatening money and grain heavily knocked on his head, and the world went black. He said it as if he was enduring some great pain:

"Forget it!"

Zhangpu

— Tian

In the countryside of southern Fujian, we often see a type of farmer who comes across as particularly simple-minded: their bodies are unusually strong and dark, their clothes are tattered, and they have a braid around the back of their heads. These are the outstanding Zhangpu laborers. Perhaps because Zhangpu is so closed off, or because the land is barren and life is difficult, they always carry a carrying pole, two hemp ropes,

Page 21

and a dry tobacco pipe inserted into their waistband, and they go out to earn a living everywhere. Especially during the summer and autumn harvest seasons, these farmers are almost everywhere. During their wandering, they are temporarily hired for labor here and there; sometimes they don't even receive a penny and are hired by landlords as long-term workers (farm laborers), or they become live-in sons-in-law in other people's families. They are so content with coarse food and simple clothing and so diligent in their work that they surpass farmers from other counties.

"Go! Hire a Zhangpu laborer at the temple entrance or on the main road!" Whenever the harvest season arrives, not only landlords and rich farmers, but even middle farmers, when they are extremely busy, will shout this. Those who don't have sons of their own often plan like this: "Zhangpu laborers are really good, let's see if we can find a young one to marry into the family! Is one really going to toil for a lifetime alone?"

Indeed, the labor power of Zhangpu workers is frighteningly resilient: they can work hard for fourteen hours a day without feeling tired. Like cattle and horses, they never express anger or sigh. Because of this, those employers have no choice but to grudgingly provide them with three meals and two snacks a day, with each meal requiring one sheng of rice.

"They're like they've just been released from prison, eating six or seven large bowls of rice!" They sometimes stick out their tongues like this, but what can be done? Where else can you hire such good workers?

Zhangpu laborers always work barefoot, regardless of whether it's a rainy day or a scorching sun. They don't sing, and they rarely talk: only after eating do they squat down and take a couple of puffs from their dry tobacco pipes. In their simple minds, the summer and autumn harvest seasons are truly like the golden age of the year. They always agree with each other beforehand and prepare carrying poles and ropes: then they set off on foot in groups of three or five towards destinations more than a hundred li away—other counties. In the past, when they were hired for a whole day, they not only had food to eat but could also earn eight mao; during that short harvest period of a month or so, ten or so yuan was easy to come by. Therefore, when they returned home, we could always see those dark and shiny smiling faces and cloth and shoes tied with rope at one end of the carrying pole. But in the past two years, they have been disappointed. No matter how they looked with pleading eyes, lowering their voices to inquire about work everywhere, it was ineffective. Moreover, wages have also dropped from eight mao to four mao. Why have those employers become so stingy? They can understand it. But they still go out to earn a living season after season, just like displaced northerners, lingeringly. Perhaps things are even worse in their hometown, or they hope that good times will come?

West Lake Spring Dawn

A painted boat gently paddles, drifting into West Lake's embrace,

Seeking plum blossoms, we tread through snow to enjoy spring. Plum blossoms and snow shine together, a scene of renewal. We see that plum blossoms occupy the most enchanting part of spring, and snowflakes fly in six-petaled formations, revealing their spirit. It is said that northern plum blossoms and southern snow are the treasures of the singing stage. We see that white snow and red plum blossoms create exquisite paintings. We remember that Princess Shouyang had plum blossom marks on her forehead. We remember Lan Guan being blocked by snow during a long expedition. We remember Mei Kai Dongge being called He Xun. We remember standing in the snow at the teacher's door, with the surname Cheng. We see that snow fills the gardens, and plum blossoms nurture jade. We see that plum blossoms bloom on the mountain ridges, like snow covering silver. We see that snowflakes like palms flutter towards the plum blossoms. We see plum blossom shadows slanting across, mistaken for snow-sweeping people. There are people who appreciate snow around the stove, with plum blossoms on the table. There are people who chew plum blossoms and boil tobacco, sculpting snow Guanyin. Know that the cold plum blossoms brave the snow and bloom in the cold. Know that admiring plum blossoms in heavy snow is precisely when the imperial messenger arrives. Sing a song, making friends with the cold plum blossoms and snow.

Movie News

About the Performance of the Chinese Translation of "Homeland"

Mr. Chen Mian and Mr. Tang Huaiqiu have very insightful decided to first select some psychological dramas with rough lines, because this way they can gain the understanding of the audience.

In fact, movies have indeed gradually made people in the Far East understand that our tragedies and comedies, broadly speaking, movies are to drama as long novels in newspapers are to literature, which is only a captivating beginning.

Mr. Chen and Tang are indeed insightful. In Beiping, Nanjing, in the interior, and in Shanghai, they selected, translated, and performed plays that were relatively easy to understand, with moving plots and solid techniques. They performed "La Traviata," a play that has been successful in Europe and America. Surprisingly, it has been promoted to China.

They are now presenting "Homeland" to everyone. Now that this play is to be performed in France, we can have many opinions. Sardou's plays were very popular between 1870 and 1914, but now we feel that he is a bit outdated. Because the technique of his plays is too perfect, every aspect of his plays has subtle calculations to arouse the audience's curiosity, but there is a lack of truly moving tones.

Sardou paid great attention to stage design and effects, which are all methods of touching the senses. The horror plays that followed used this formula. Although "Homeland" does not actually show the scene of secret trials and executions, we can hear the cries of the victims, and the red light outside the window in one scene of "Homeland" can make us imagine the burning pile of firewood, but these effective methods can only be loved by the audience for a short time.

Sardou was the most authoritative figure in the French theater scene for forty years. Now, his "Madame Sans-Gêne" still has great appeal. Sardou is not only a technical writer, he also has soul, interest, and subtle observation. His comedies, which are now forgotten, should not be forgotten because his comedies are indeed stronger than his tragedies. If his "Rabagas," this immortal comedy, were performed by a director like Charles Dullin, who would dare to say that it would not be a sensation? It is also that our customs have changed, and "Rabagas," which could cause a stir sixty years ago, can no longer surprise our audience.

In any case, Sardou, who could still excite all of Paris with the play "The Poison Affair" in the same year, will surely be welcomed by the Chinese people, because they have not yet become tired of this technique. Moreover, his technique does have recognizably good value, and the patriotic ideals contained in "Homeland" should be sympathized with by Chinese youth.

Mr. Chen Mian and Mr. Tang Huaiqiu's efforts are worthy of our double admiration, because they are introducing our theatrical art to their compatriots, and they are working hard to create new plays. Our country adds a new and individualistic art. (The End) (Translated from the Shanghai French Daily, September 10th)

Runaway Marriage

Showing in Nanjing

"Mr. Wang's Chivalrous Adventures" Has a Pure Theme

Director Zuo Ming's "Mr. Wang's Chivalrous Adventures" has been released at the Jincheng Grand Theater since the 17th. This is a film that takes a realistic theme in the form of a comedy and points out a bright path for the audience. Director Zuo used his new style to expose the dark side and strange phenomena of society, such as the treachery of people's hearts, the suffering of laborers, the ugliness of false patriots, and the dreams of small property owners, which can be said to have exhausted the ability of humor and satire.

Because "Mr. Wang's Chivalrous Adventures" is performed in the form of a comedy, the whole film is full of hilarious jokes, but its theme is so pure and its meaning is so great that the audience will have serious aftertastes after laughing.

Chatting About "Carnival Night"

"Carnival Night" is another great contribution of Xinhua Company after "Peach Blossom Spring Dream."

"Carnival Night" is Shi Dongshan's exquisite masterpiece after "Song of Everlasting Sorrow."

The stars of "Carnival Night" are Hu Ping, Jin Shan, Gu Eryi, Zhou Xuan, Yin Xiuqin, Gu Menghu, Shi Chao, Jiang Xiu, You Guanren, etc., who have a very deep history in film and stage.

"Carnival Night" is adapted from the famous play "The Inspector General" written by the great Russian writer Gogol, which is a work with very beautiful and profound meaning.

"Carnival Night" is a vicious satire on corrupt politics.

"Carnival Night" is a powerful bomb thrown at the officialdom of flattery and oppression.

The dialogue in "Carnival Night" is very witty and humorous, making people excited and stimulated.

"Carnival Night" is full of not noisy slapstick, making you laugh and angry.
